O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Your voice, three dear sons, I have completed this book which is the last part of the science of assembled medicine and have finished it through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I would complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and is estranged from top to bottom, thus the science has perished and is decayed, and there remains nothing more of the fuels than the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes the error and the vanity, and the intentions are closed and the science is estranged.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I want to revive the ordering of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will assemble the forms of the iron instruments of cautery, and of the other instruments of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands were found in our time, is the art of medicine extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for the one who undertakes to thoroughly learn the science of anatomy, as Galien says, so that he knows the judgment of the members, and the forms and conjunctions and separations of them, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and brains and the number of them, and their movement and rest, and how they issue from there.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And for this reason said Hippocrates that the name is not much with the name, and with the work is little;
et meismement en l’art de main.	and similarly in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We say in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned before, if he is not careful he will fall into error and harm people.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Therefore I have seen many of those who practice this science and abandon their sense and their experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a foolish doctor who cut into an abscess or swelling on a woman's neck, and cut the arteries of the neck.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood flows out that the woman falls dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another mirror who treated a stone of a man's urine, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	he took away with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if they had operated on him, he would have died.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another mirror who took in care the duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the breakage he had a wound;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the mirror blamed ignorance for holding the breakage against the wound with very strong binding, and did not leave the wound any discharge, and thus he left it in this condition;
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he ordered that it should not be dislocated again;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and thus it remained until the leg was completely swollen and the foot, and came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I am called to come to him, and I hurry to come to release his leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I saw it dislocated thus it was in a country and he did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But all the way the corruption was already confirmed on the limb, and I could not heal it;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and the corruption did not cease to spread through the limb so that the entire limb became almost entirely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And he saw another doctor who burst open an abscess that was hidden, and then it became inflamed due to the evil of his lordship's malice.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For cancer, when it is pure melancholic humor, it does not seem that one should touch with iron unless the place is entirely clean so that one can remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	it is to know, whether there is danger in many dispositions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Because it is necessary that you beware, so that foolish mirrors cannot speak badly of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take your arms in a cross, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way that for God's grace you come to health and be praised.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the maladies to reveal the grievous sanity;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and lift your arms from that which makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may be able to come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen says among some of his warnings:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take on the care of a bad disease, lest you be called foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are about fire cauterization and medicinal cauterization, and these chapters are arranged from the head to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and about the forms of instruments, and the iron tools of cauterization, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and suction cups and wounds, and extracting arrows, and similar things;
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and it is the ordered chapters and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it is ordered according to the lower head just as feet, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Here is the translation:
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of aid, and the harm, are the longest words and subtle science and the secret responses;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and from these they speak of the wisest men, and agree with them;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and I suffer little from their words, for I reduce the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that fire cautery universally aids every complexion where there is matter, before the two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	it is to know warm temperament without material, and dry temperament without material.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In warm and dry temperaments together with material, they devised none and said that cautery is a great aid;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that cautery is of no value for an illness that comes from chill and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is warm, and it should not be used to cure a warm illness through chill, nor through dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and he said that those who say the opposite, that cautery makes great aid to warm and dry illnesses that come in the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you examine the body of the man and its moisture according to the complexions of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true many times through experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in no way, one should not interfere with those who have experienced it, and who know through long usage the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the events and the space of time;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	of other complexions we have not so much fear, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the mirrors assemble and agree with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that fire cautery is one of the secrets of cures, and of greater goodness than medicine burning with ardor.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come except to the member that is cooked, and does not harm another member if it is not named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	The fiery remedies pass from one member to another by transmitting, and bring the diseased limb to a grievous sanitation;
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and sometimes kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire, because of its height and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found by experiment and through the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is established on the truth of things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for this I excuse myself from the length of the speech, because it does not please me that I withhold the secret which is hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives out the diseases of the body, as the philosopher said in demonstrating.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	for you receive in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agree at the time when they should be done, the cauteries, and choose promptly.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is suitable at all times, because the sudden injuries that occur are easily cured by the aid of cautery;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and meanwhile the cauteries are for necessary pains and swift ones that cannot wait for the time when greater evil may come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And do not think of anything, dear son, if you make the foolish mirror;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the illness that is healed by cautery has no relapse;
et il le dient ensi;	and they say it thus;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not so as they think, because cauteries are not just a medicine that changes the complexion, and dries the humors that are the cause of pain, and is more valuable than medicine for the speed of its effect, and for the virtue of its work and its dominion.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible that the disease comes at some time according to the temperament of the patient and the location of the illness and its power.
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and are gathered in him the excesses through the acquisition of foods and similar things, if it is not cauterized in a place where there is little excess and moisture, just as cauterization is administered for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return;
mais ce avient poc.	but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and that is true.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cauterization is valuable after medicine, but their intentions are false, and it is cauterization the last resort of medicine because when we administer methods of cures for any illness and they do not work, then we administer cauterization, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it appears clearly that cauteries are the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancient ones said that cauteries of gold instrument are more effective than those of iron, and they did not say this because of the quality of gold and because of the height of its substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that the eyes of the cautery do not make a bad wound, but this is not true because I have experienced it, and I have found that it is true in some men;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and cauteries of gold are worth more than those of iron, as they said loudly.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And always when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is heated by the color of gold, and it is quickly cooled;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if one heats it too much;
si font au feu;	they make at the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus there is enough of impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we do not use cautery of iron that we have not made appear in our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have ordered this chapter concerning the wounded head just below, because the way is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Fire cautery is good for moisture and coldness on the brain, and it is used for the cause of an illness called "soda", and because of many humors that descend to the head as eyes, and ears, and for a multitude of sounds and pain in the teeth and pain in the throat, and also for all illnesses that come from coldness such as paralysis, sodic and apoplectic diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by solvent medicine modifying the head three or four times, according to whether the strength and the age and the habituation of the patient can suffer it;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then make the patient's head steady.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on your thighs;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	afterwards put the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and there where your two fingers meet, if it bleeds from the notch then heat the cautery which is called "olivare", because that is its form;
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the marked spot of ink, and do so by descending and extracting your hand little by little while twisting;
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then lift your hand slowly, and reward the spot if you see the bone I small;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, restart the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	afterwards take a little silk, and place it in warm and soft cotton inside, and place it on the spot, and let it be for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	after putting a soft cloth in a pouch;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and let it be until the inflammation is reduced;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing the wound of the joint which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the old men said that the more one delays opening the wound, the more it suppurates;
et por ce si aide mues.	and therefore it is helped little by little.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said that one should not leave the cautery so long that part of the bone is burned, and then reset what is burned of the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And the others say that one should cauterize as long as one leaves it on, and thrust so strongly that one abates from the bone as wide as the veil that women put in their hair to collect the humors that issue forth;
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one should leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	afterwards one should cure and sew it up.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two manners of cauterization do not seem to me to be good at all, unless in some men where there is a way of fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I should let them grow;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the head is weakened by continuous natural solutions, as we demonstrate in other limbs;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and also when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more healing and soothing for me, and that's why I often work together in harmony for health.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain at the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When the entire head comes with chronic pain, and lasts a long time, then one should use the patient's remedies of ghee and pills that are called "cochie", and purging of the head and eyes and applying plasters;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one performs the cautery that we mentioned before, it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care that the head of the patient is of strong nature, and that it is not too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize beneath that one, a little of what we said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After performing fire cautery on each horn-like prominence of the head just to the bone, as we have said before, and perform the cautery where it is called "vasels".
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and it is the joints in which one puts ventoses;
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and elevate your hand so that you do not touch just to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patients feel too much greater pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the cauteries of the horns be more subtle than those with which one cauterizes the softness of the head, and this is the method:
dou cautere dou chief	for fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When in one part of the head sudden pain comes, and the disease is extended to the eye, and the head is purged by Mondificent medicines, and other cures that I have said in the division of diseases are made, and all this does not profit:
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	then you do cauteries according to two methods, namely knowing of medicinal heat and of iron.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The cauteries of medicinal heat are that you take a bundle of hot ashes, and remove the scorching and recoat it with a little powder on the heads, and then make a temple where the pain holds in such manner that you may reposition the bundle of hot ashes beneath the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is repositioned, bind it and hold it well and leave it thus for 12 hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then unbind it and draw forth the bundle of hot ashes, and leave the wound thus for 2 or 3 days;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then put on a cotton dressing soaked in water so that it penetrates to the bone.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the treatment of the wound until it be sound;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see that I have written about some burning medicines or twelve treatises on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery to where it is in the form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a nail or it has little curvature, and appears small in appearance;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand and twist the iron a little more gently, so that most of the skin where the burn is should be eased;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and lift your hand so the artery does not become hard, which is of no use, and abundance of blood will flow out.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	Afterwards apply cotton to the wound, and place it on the spot for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply moistened cotton to the wound, and then treat the spot with ointment until it is healthy;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this emigraine with the cautery that is called "cultellare", at all points, and beware of cutting the artery in this emigraine which is not ancient.
de emigraine	of the emigraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat migraines as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases, and do not profit from it, and see that the cauteries previously mentioned in medicine and iron do not suffice for him, then it is necessary to burn the cautery which is called "cultellare" so that it is white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and sign thus on the dull eye a line of half a finger's length, and lift your hand once, and hold it so that you do not touch the artery and do not reach just to the bone;
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	and beware of the mandible that moves when one chews, and the nerves do not have regard for the movement and that spasm does not come to the patient, and beware of the disruption of blood from the artery when it is touched, where touching has great fear and mistrust in him who does not know himself, and who is not a student and experienced;
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and let the vein be in my way;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to staunch blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you in this book where it happens.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that these cauteries do not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the enemy at the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healthy;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two edges;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and these are better cauteries than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	from the pain of the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear from cold, and we have applied solutive medicines and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pains do not move, then heat this cautery which is called "points", of which this is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After puncturing all around the ailing ear, or around the two where the pain takes hold in both, and you will separate a little below the root of the ear before you have signed the place of the incision;
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and let there be ten points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing, let the limb be sound.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Pains that must be treated with cauterization are not fiercer than those that move with flux, as we have said in the divisions of diseases;
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not apply cauterization to similar things that come from dryness and spasms of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this kind of pain that moves with flux of waters and purgings of head and gurgling, and it does not work, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauterizations:
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, and another a little above the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and put the cauterization on the part that appears healthy, and make it cauterized at the top of the ear a little below the crown of the head, and another in the temple as long as a thumb;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and let the cautery iron remain on the skin as long as the heat of the heart is felt;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and that is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it is similar to the scalpel that we have placed beforehand, but it is a bit more subtle and requires that the cuts be a bit larger;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing the wound, let it be as I said before, until it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When the apoplexy is ancient and you treat it as we have said, and it does not profit, and the patient has no fever, then you make four cauteries:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one on the spot called "vassels" as we have said before, and the fourth cautery on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and let it be cured as we have said before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this disease, it is necessary to give the patient large draughts and pills that purify the brain;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	afterwards place on the patient's head a plaster of mustard which is written or treated in treatises on plasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the manner of cauterizing:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if you do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If he is thus healthy, it is good;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if he is not, make three cauterizations on the skin of his head descending to the neck, and leave a space between each cauterization of two fingers' width;
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and treat him as the others, and if you see that he is troubled, and the patient is suffering, make one cauterization in the middle;
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the mastery is, two others on the two horns, and treat until he is healthy;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cautery which is called "olivare" be, as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	from the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be treated with years and with what we have said before;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	afterwards treat the head of the patient, then make a cautery in the head and on each horn, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you have more mastery, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is strong, then make four cauteries on the spine of the back;
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and let it be until the worst heat is absorbed, and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the treatment until he is healthy, and let the cautery which is called "olivare" that we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	from epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to moisturize the brain with years and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the disease is great and suffers from taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is an infant who cannot yet suffer, then make a gargling and mastication soothing the brain often with good foods;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the king's arm is set in a circle, and you make the fire cautery according to what we have said before, and apply the fire cautery on the little vessel, and on each corner.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is strong and suffers, make fire cauteries as I have said to those who are paralyzed and have softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the olive-tree fire cautery be according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, make them undergo subtle cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When the cause of melancholy is excessive or corrupt and gross humors, then apply the cautery of such cauteries as we said for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the cause of melancholy is excessive humors declining into melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that will cleanse their brain according to what was said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After setting the head of the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	after making the well-made lint tourniquet, just like a circle, if you put it on his head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the patient will be crossed, and be well held from all parts;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	after applying the bandage, and wrap with a layer of old heather berries;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and heat it with tempered fire, so that the fingers can endure the pain of the poultice.
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	After seeing the circle deep within the head, let it cool down.
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this for the patient every week once with another good government, as long as he is healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Where you see that you are cauterizing, make points more often throughout the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This manner of cautery softens the brain equally;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then put on cotton wool moistened with butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	from the warmth of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When warmth comes first to the eyes through the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and give drink to the patient something warming the head, and the guard against all moisture, and let them sweat or bathe many times a day.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	Afterwards, command him to shave his head, and make him undergo cautery within the head, and apply two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of the brain is in both eyes, or if the descent is in one eye.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and cut all the cauteries to all the veins and arteries that are beneath the heart, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple.
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and beware of the flow of blood, and if you see too much blood issuing, then staunch it with a piece of cloth as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and incising cautery how you will anesthetize it;
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and sometimes one makes a cautery or heats it beneath the two back bones.
dou cors des larmes	because of the course of the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or beneath the arteries that appear at the top of the forehead;
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and one sees that it is from the cold, phlegmatic superfluities, then he makes the cautery that I spoke of at the beginning of the treatise descending to the eyes;
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I make a cautery in the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or heating beneath the two back bones;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if it is more bothersome, then one should cauterize gently above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	They burn the tears back behind the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you medicate according to what we have said in the division, and it does not profit at all, then give three bad drinks to the patient.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	after the king's head, and make a cautery or a thousand gold cauteries;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and make two cauteries of the cautery that is called "clavulis" on the two sorrows, a little below the eyebrows;
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and beware of the artery that you do not touch it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery that is called "clavulis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the pupil of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize with this cautery which is called "olivary".
de coi ci est li forme:	of where it is in the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see that make two cauteries on the two sorrows as long as the sorcils are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not leave your hand there unless the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	It never happens that the hair of the eyes is converted to baldness, and pricks the eye, and one makes cauteries according to two methods:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	It is to know of fire, or of burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they grow and are even, then put the patient in a healthy state;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	after marking on the paper of the eyes a figure that is just like the pattern of a dead man's brain, and let it be the beginning of the sign from the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then put a cotton wool moistened with egg white and powder of pearl on the eye, then heat the cautery to the form that it is;
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterizing on the figure that you have marked, little by little, many times, so that the vein is burned in that place;
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of health in the skin are that you see the parchment-like skin drawn back, and the hairs rise to the point of the eye;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then lift your hand, and let it be for three days, then I put moist cotton in a bag until the inflammation is removed;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of the joint until it is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And if after that the hairs grow, and the parchment-like skin is softened, then recommence the cautery on the same spot, just as you did previously;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	and if the hairs are burnt, then cauterize until the parchment-like skin is raised to its natural level, and is even, and does not prick the eye with the hairs.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The fiery medical cauteries are that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow as long and even as they can be, then make a parchment in the shape of the leaf of myrtle.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	Then take French soap and lively chalk, a dot of each, and crush them well together;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and make it hastily, so that it doesn't cool, then spread it on the form you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and put it on the paper of eyes;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the disease holds in one only solacement, one must open in one, and if it is ambidextrous also;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and put beneath the eye a cotton wad moistened with egg white;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and let the head of the patient be in your health and put your finger showing on the medicine, and press the poultice and move it every time the patient feels biting from the medicine, for it feels biting as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then apply the medicine to your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the biting is past, lift the lever of awe, and reward yourself if you see the paper lifted also as it was lifted by constraint of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is thus, it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If this is not so, reset the medicine on the wound or the medicine has not worked, until your workings are even, and your eyes are set in place;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a cotton molliet in a poultice until the harsh corrosions are soothed, after curing the wound of the joint which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it be healthy.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And it is necessary for you to take great care with your work by great diligence so that there is no neglect in the medicine of the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the skin becomes soft afterwards, and the hair pricks in the eye, then recommence the medicine on that wound which is softened by the proper paper, thus as you have done before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the cure until it be healthy.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and that is the form of the leaf of dead myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in greatness and in smallness, and according to that be your constraints;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and let it not deviate from the right path for him who is studying this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, then it is necessary to perform cautery according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to put his head in a healthy position;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor nod its head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	afterwards apply a cotton wool moistened with the juice of a pear or the milk of a peach on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	afterwards heat the cautery which is thus:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it is shaped at the head like the form of a hollow pen, together with which it is the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you see, it should be pointed from one part of the head to the other, and if you see, it should also be like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but anyway, this which is shaped is of no value for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing on the fistula it is uncovered, and one removes the putridity, and the dryness.
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	and it is closed, if it opens, and one removes the false bottom;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	after placing the hot iron on the cauterized area, and holding your hand on the cauterizing iron at the part of the nail where it meets the eye, so that your hand does not make a fool;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	and place the cauterizing iron in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If this does not work, then recommence the cauterizing iron once more, and if you are not a master of it, leave it for three days;
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	after I put on a cotton molliet in a poultice, and cure the ointment of the desiccative until it is healthy, and if forty days pass without it being healthy, then I put on medicine against corrosive ulcers so that the bone may be uncovered;
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	and let him rest according to what he needs in his chamber.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a type of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Then make a fistula, and bend the limb;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	after putting in the incision, I insert a subtle CAM (instrument) according to where it is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and they make a quantity of an ounce of lead;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	and hold your hand or instrument firmly, and do not move the patient at all, so that the melted lead does not run to his eye;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	and it is necessary to put on the patient's eye a cotton wad soaked in egg whites or in water;
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	the melted lead thus forms the shape of a fistula, and the healthy part marvelously regains its health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healthy through the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then one must administer poultices to the nave, and bring the fistula back to its proper place according to what is necessary for its own site.
des crevaices en levres	of cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks occur on the lips that are called "hairs", and similarly on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks with what we have said in sections, and the treatment does not profit, then you should use a small cautery tool according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font;	And apply it hastily to those cavities as far as life comes forth;
aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	after curing the limb of corrosion until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the gullet
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the eye, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth, after it has made putridity and rot and is inflamed and becomes fistulous;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not benefit at all:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	then it is necessary that you have cauterization according to the quantity of the fistula;
aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu;	after the opening or perforation of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron tip comes to the front of it, and where the rear of the hand;
et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do thus one or two times, after the treatment of what we have said in treatments, until it be healthy;
et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin;	and if it is treated thus, it is good;
et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	and if not, then it is necessary to discover the place and cut out the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines but it doesn't work, then put the patient's head in a healthy position.
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	After heating the cautery whose form will come thus afterwards in such a way that you put a chain over the tooth.
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	and place the hot cautery hastily, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth.
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	After lifting your hand and recommencing the cautery according to your will.
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	After filling the patient's mouth with salty water, and holding it for an hour and then blowing fiercely.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner the teeth which were moving are confirmed, and the gums are softened restrained, and the moisture corrupts the scab.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold or glass, and medical treatments are of no value, then it is necessary to use cautery according to the two methods.
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and burning cauterization and fire cauterization.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	Burning cauterization is such that you hold a burning iron in a holder of iron or copper;
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent, and dip it in burning bull's fire, and place it on the aching tooth quickly and hold until it cools down;
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	and thus do often until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that it puts a cold flame and cotton in burning frost, and place on the aching tooth, and place on the hot iron as far as the fire reaches the decay of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The cauterization with fire is such that you hold a iron rod or copper, and it should be thick so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth;
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After burning with fire cautery, because of this the wound forms a crust that way afterwards, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand so long as the cautery cools down.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, for the pain will be alleviated that same day or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good warm water in the impression of that cautery, and then he spits it out forcibly.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of a good cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And make a good cautery on the part that you want, and according to what you are able.
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the form of the burn:
des scrophules	of the scalp ulcers
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrophules are of flux and cold moistures, and do not obey digestion by medicines, then burn with fire cautery, because afterwards it forms a crust, and it has two openings for the fumes to exit from the cautery on the other part.
et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume;	and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, where it is most needed, until it reaches the root of the abscess;
et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors;	and if the abscess is small, then place the cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and let it be for three days;
et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee;	and put on a cotton cloth soaked in butter until the discharge is eliminated;
aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	after curing, anoint the limb with ointments and tents until it is healthy.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the chain:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives;	When moisture accumulates on the channels of the arm, and similarly when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first with dissolving medicines;
aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	after you do cautery at the root of the throat, and take care that you do not come too close to the throat, and do not cauterize with a hot iron but rather a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant;	After the fire cautery, apply another cautery to the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and it is the cautery that is called "clavicle" because we have the shape in front.
et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal the limb as we have said before, so that it may be healthy.
de la toust	of the thumb
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai .II cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis;	When all the diseases of the chest are from cold and moist vapors, and the patients have no fever nor cough, and it is a chronic disease, then apply two cauteries to the strength in their veins.
et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles;	and another cautery between the nipples.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	and it is the cautery that is called "clavicle" according to the shape that has been mentioned before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles;	And if you see, apply cautery by pricking to the entire cautery that is called "points" because the shape is thus before in the disease of the ears.
et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	and let the hairs grow just up to XXX, or thereabouts.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After healing the limb according to what has been said before, and let the cauteries be at three points according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because they are lighter cauterizations, because you make them in three places at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit;	Then let the patient turn onto his back and onto his side;
aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre;	then lift the heart that is within the little finger of your left hand;
et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	and if the joint is dislocated within, then heat the cautery that has two nerves where it is in the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres;	and cauterize the heart as much as it pierces just up to the side, and there would come the figure of three cauteries assembled with four cauteries;
et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres;	and for this reason, cautery is made with the cautery that has three nerves, because the figures of cauterization are six cauteries;
et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and they are the nerve according to the subtlety of a tendon, and it is the form of the cautery that has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And often is applied on this same nerve because it has eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil;	Then put on the cautery, pricking the burned area with a needle;
aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After having put the patient at rest, do not touch the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, little things happen, then do cautery on the thick part of the cautery nail, or many cauteries in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed again, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach coldness and much moisture occur until it affects his complexion, and multiple cathartics are given to him, and accustomed methods of cure do not profit, then it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back, and stretches out his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture;	From these, afterwards make three fire cauterizations in the hollow of the thigh according to the quantity of a finger, with each entire cauterization being at an angle, and there should be space between one and another so they are not joined together when they form a triangle.
et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	and let the cauterization be so profound that it reaches the two parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauterizations be according to this form without adjustment.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme;	And if you see a large cauterization in the stomach according to this form;
et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche;	and he who will have fear of this cauterization, let him cauterize by pricking and signing on the stomach at that point according to the quantity that you see of an inch.
puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	then the cauterizer applies all the cauterization which is called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound that we have had before, until it be healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez;	When the liver suffers from cold and moisture and great windiness, so that it is far removed from its natural complexion through excesses;
et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil;	and the patient is cured of what we have said in divisions, and it does not profit him, if it is necessary that the patient be anointed on his ulcer;
et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient;	and make three cauterizations according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, below the hypochondries, where the humor or the parts of the omere come;
et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi;	and let there be a space between each cauterization the width of a finger;
et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere;	and let the cauterizations be two fingers' length from the body, and do not press too hard with your hand on the entire cauterization;
et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez;	and let it be burned as much as the middle of the heart, and let the patient stand upright on their feet;
et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais;	and if he cannot, then let him lean, and stretch out his legs, and lift his arms;
et c’est li forme:	and that is the posture:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors;	And if you want to, then cauterize these cauteries of the cuticular, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn the whole heart, for you would make it drier than the whole body;
et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	and that it does not come near the bowel, for the heart is very subtle there, and one should beware of seeing;
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile:	When there is an abscess on the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane:
s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort;	if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too excessively strong;
et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	and if he is in a bandage, he feels foreign pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste;	And when this treatment affects the mirrors, it is necessary that the patient be warned about his head;
et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	and then sign where the abscess or swelling is, and then heat the cautery that is similar to the reason, from which it is the shape:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers;	And cauterize with the cautery as much as the veins are burnt, and approach just to the siphac, until the pores are completely purified;
aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez;	after the treatment, according to the treatment of the humors, until he is healthy;
et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	and it is not suitable that anyone use this cautery unless he who has studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and whose hands these diseases have corrected many times.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then it can hardly work, and yet it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere:	The ancients said that one should make multiple cauteries at the roots of aristology, and in such a manner:
pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a root of aristology as long as you can find it, the largest one possible, and let it be dry, and let it also be as thick and as long as your fingers.
