et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and grind it in oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize with a cautery between the shoulder blade and the neck, and apply small cauteries a little downward on the part that is beneath the beard.
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	and apply cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining backward a little.
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	and apply a cautery in the thigh, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on both sides of the thigh, opposite the cautery that is between the shoulders.
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	and do not press with your hand, but rather make an opening as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And some old men said that no one uses fire cautery similar to a razor, and they heat it up and place it between the ribs, until it reaches the abscess.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	and thus the pain flees, as we have said in the aposteme of the foolish fever.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear where the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the spleen
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the spleen according to what we have said as divisions of treatments, and it does not profit at all, then they perform three manners of fire cautery that are good for everything.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant;	Since it is a manner that you make three cauterizations, or four, in a line according to the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the cautery of the foolish fever that we have said before.
et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	and do not press your hand on all the cauterizations, and let the patient be warned to lie on their back;
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule;	and another manner of cauterization is that you heat the cautery which has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder;
et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	and lift the heart which is near the mouse, or where the stitches of the patient come from the left, and let the elevations that you lift the heart according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cautery should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII.	After they burn the two nerves as much as the heart is perceived from the other side, and then they will make three incisions with the cautery, and thus there will be four.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	And if you see that, if you cauterize the entire cautery at three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has been obtained by lengthy tension, and this is more than the other cures mentioned beforehand.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Fire cautery is not suitable for dropsy, except in the manner that is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you treat it according to the methods that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not profit at all, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the bowels, and one above the stomach, and one above the liver, and one above the spleen, and two behind the back on the spine, and one on the pis.
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	and let the cauteries be well close to the thickness of a finger.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	Afterwards, leave the cautery open for a long time to allow for putrid matter to flow out, and do not stop the treatment of the patient after the cautery.
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	and healing will hasten, and the two intentions will be assembled with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	The shape of the cautery for the belly should be the key that we have placed before demonstrating;
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what is placed here before us.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the inflammation of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical, and are full of citrine water, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the auricular and the anular;
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply in the fontanelle, lest it would force out the bitter humor, and let the cauterization be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	Afterwards, make two cauteries on each leg at the point of the cuticular.
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	and let the cauteries be of a length, one beneath the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg.
et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse;	and leave the cauteries on for a long time without removing them, so that the water may issue forth.
aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	after the treatment of other treatments that we have said.
de la menoison	of the swelling
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures;	When a belly problem comes from cold and moisture, so that the retaining and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines are afflicted, and cannot be cured by ways of treatments;
et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule;	and you see the patient suffering greatly and of strong virtue, if you do the great cautery on the stomach according to what has been spoken of before, or cautery of the stomach, with circular cautery;
et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	and 4 cauteries around the subtle bowel for all subtle cautery, and 3 cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abounding and the patient suffering, make him a cautery on the finger, and one cautery on each rib, and two small cauteries on the stomach beneath the great one, for the cure is profitable when it has good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres:	When the hemorrhoids are in the foundation, or one or more, and are ancient and are of gross cold and moist humors corrupted, and are cured as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit at all, if you do cauteries:
III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois;	On the spine of the back, which is all deformed below the shoulder blade, and slightly in a triangle shape, and I apply fire cautery on the nodule that is there.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile;	and if you think that the stomach is chilled, and the food does not digest, and one sees the face swell, then one applies a great fire cautery on the stomach, as it was said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with all the fire cautery of the clave;
et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	and let the fire cautery remain on for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing the limb so that it becomes healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is named "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit;	When you touch the scar, heat up the fire cautery that seems to rasp, and then apply it all burned onto the touched scar.
et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort;	and leave your hand so long as the fire cautery reaches the birth of the vein, from which the blood flows out.
fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit;	do this once or twice, and if there is much of the scar, cauterize each one as we have said.
aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez;	after the treatment of eye problems as long as they are healthy;
et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the skin, it will have even greater help.
de plaie mal curee	of a badly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure a surgical procedure or an operation, which we will describe in its place, then comes such a disease that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a fistula comes, and it is wrapped and casts putrid and corrupt moisture, if you prove all of it under a subtle tent, and beware that you know all of the tent how deep it has penetrated.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing;	After heating the cautery that seems to be a razor, and put it in the fistula according to the quantity that the tension is entered, and recommence the cautery as long as the corrupted and rotten body parts are burned, one time, or two, or three, according to the quantity of their need.
et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	and guard against burning the nerves that are affected, and the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans;	if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and to the intestine, so guard against these evils, and do not make those false fires that are in the charned flesh, and think that it is not almost pierced.
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement;	after treating the flesh as long as it is healthy, and if the flesh is healed, and the materials are removed at length of time, then know that the flesh is entirely healthy.
et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font;	and if the materials are not removed, it means that the joints are twisted, and the bones are corrupted at the source;
et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	and thus like one of those which we will direct to its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit;	When pain from cold comes to the roots, and from great windiness, and does not take heed of a woman, then it is necessary that you perform cauterization on the roots from one side and another at the clavicle cauterization which we mentioned before.
et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauterizations in a line, and they will bring greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce;	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then make cauterization on the outer part above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic region begin, and one on the right and one on the left, and each cauterization should be as long as our thumb.
et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing;	and have them cauterize the back, where they will need an assistant;
et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	and let the cautery iron be formed according to the aforementioned shape.
de la marris	of the marrow
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde;	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow conception for that reason, and the flowers are corrupted and their endings delayed;
et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor:	and when they come, they feel great pain:
adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos;	then it is necessary to perform three cauteries around the belly, as we have said about the cautery of the bladder, and they will cauterize the back;
et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	and let the cautery iron be shaped, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble;	When the moist viscous humors descend to the hollow of the thigh, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measuring them together;
et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle;	and it is found that the joints of the division are visible, so it is necessary that you cauterize the patient on the box of the hip according to the cautery similar to a circle, and mark in front of the joint within the box as it turns, so that the box is inside the circle;
et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	and if the cauteries are such as those with which one has cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs;	And if these cauteries are not present to you, make three cauteries of the large olivary, and let the cauteries be as profound as all the veins.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until he is healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	from the pain of the ankle
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain comes to the box of the hip, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is treated for what we have said in the division and the treatment is not effective, and the disease is ancient:
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	then it is necessary to purge the patient of thick, foul humors of fetid pills or other similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere;	After the fire cautery;
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	and the manner of doing cautery is according to two manners:
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	it is to know that it assembles burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cautery is according to many manners, of which one is such:
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	that you cauterize on the surface of the thigh three triangular cauteries according to this form, and it makes good depth and greatness, and has between each cauterization a space the thickness of a finger, and so the cauteries are olive-shaped;
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	sometimes one makes a cauterization in the middle on the head of the thigh, because there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	And if you see, it is cauterized at the circular cauterization that we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the thigh;
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	but do it in such a manner that the circles encompass the entire thigh, and all the spaces of the heart should be burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And that is the manner in which they do it for sciatica, when the pain holds in the thigh, and does not reach as far as the knee or as far as the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it reaches the thigh and leg, have two fire cauteries there where the patient says the pain holds them, and three fire cauteries above the ankle, on the left side a little.
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	and let the cautery be cuticular, and let the spaces of the heart be burned;
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two toes of the foot or near there, then cauterize where they feel the pain three points or four at the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if it is necessary, have them do more.
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	and if it is known that the pain is beneath the knee towards the thigh, have them do a fire cautery at the cuticular or circular cautery, and take great care in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery so much that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more great nuisance and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have seen many who have undergone cauterization on the thigh, and they left it so long that the leg became completely swollen, and the foot as well, and was pierced and corrupted throughout the foot.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a flux of belly which led him to death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, perform cauterization on one and the other, according to this method.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the wise men said about the cautery of the thigh, that it is in this manner, make the iron thus sharp and be at the tip as big as a thumb's nail, or a little less, and be by inserting and be from one insertion to another spacing out the quantity of a ninth of an inch.
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	and let the insertions be above two fingers' breadth, and let them also be like knots, and have the iron handle well made;
et c’est li forme:	and that is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	And let it be heated until it is totally red hot and gives off sparks, and then place it on the affected thigh's boil, and turn it on the healthy side;
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	and let it cauterize once, and then remove the cautery and leave it for three days;
et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens;	and then apply a poultice of butter, and leave the wound uncovered for a long time;
aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment of joint so that it be healthy.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery for fear of his regard, and we see few who use it.
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	and yet these are good cauteries, which can soothe, and there where they are applied.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The burning cauteries of medicine are so that you make the instrument at a stretch between the margins of the door, and it is either of iron or copper with a long handle, and in its height it has two points, and each has the quantity of the thickness of a finger.
et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	and be open above and below, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	After put on the box of the hip to the ailing person lying on his healthy side, and then place your hand much on the box of the hip.
aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After the hand is placed between the two circles of warm water which has been heated by fire in a small pot, and let it stay for an hour of gentle heat, and the patient suffers from chill and numbness.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu;	For it is true that he finds biting pain as if from fire;
et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit;	and when the biting pains have passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the warm water of sweet dew, and let it stay thus for three days, and apply a poultice so that what is black from the burn may be removed;
et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait;	and let it stay three days until the pus flows out in a stream;
et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	and that would be the last aid after the treatment of wounds, so that they may be healthy.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument;	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or to the leg, make an instrument that holds warm water according to what you have done in the wound just so;
et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	and it is the manner of warm water, and I have written it in a treatise on the rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take equal parts of alkaline and living chalk, as much of one as of the other, and crush them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir;	where there is a small opening to be made so that the tip of a scalpel can enter;
et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main;	and put on top of that pot another well-plumbed pot, and put on alkaline and chalk and warm water above, until there is a duo of powders underneath which you will have well prepared in your hand;
et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	and let it sit until it descends into warm water and reaches the well-plumbed pot, then take all that water, and pour it over chalk and alkaline as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres.	And then it will be very warm and is administered in many works of medicine and in cauterizations of other members.
Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	For it does other works like fires, and if there are other medicines where one cauterizes well the thigh thus as thesis and honey and alkaline and soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galien tells us about a cure where one man was cured of the pain in his hainche and sciatic vein, and he limped greatly, and said that there was no other cure, and that he was healed at once when this cure was done, and he was bathed as it is taught afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And thus in this manner you should take the green fresh and dry litargire, and crush it much with a little fat, and apply it to the thigh and to the knee and to the leg where the pain lies, and the relief.
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	and let it be for three hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the bitterness.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	Then have him enter a warm bath so that his body is slightly relaxed, and have him enter bed, and the pain will all go away and he will be healthy.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire cautery with such medicines, unless it's after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dyascorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with hot iron, it helps much;
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and it should be done by making the cauteries in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take a linen cloth and the warmth of old oil, and apply it to the fossa that is between the thumb of the foot and the other called fascia.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After taking dry hot iron, and heating it in the fire until it becomes charcoal, and applying it to the loin, and leaving it there until it is extinguished;
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and do it again thus, and do not cease from doing thus until you think by sense that it comes just to the thigh, and that the pain is ceased;
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	and this manner of cautery is called "cautery of the vein".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from a fall or percussion or by too great an evacuation, or by similar matter expanded cold, none of these appearances is worthy of cauterization, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is necessary after that the patient is void of foul pills or other similar things, that one makes on their back, there where the pain holds, three lines signed with an inch, and in each line V cauteries or more according to the strength and quantity that the patient can suffer.
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	and let the cauteries be made according to the cautery which is called "points".
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	and if you see, make three or four cauteries at the claveable cautery of the middle finger according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	Many times this illness comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a constricted arm when they get up, and fear.
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you find in the posterior spine of the back and in the appearance that comes upon the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you want to cure it, if you cauterize with the fire cautery according to this method.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	When the fire cautery burns each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, if you cauterize around the spine with a piercing fire cautery in two or three lines, and the points are close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After healing the limb so that it is healthy according to what we have said, and beware that you do not misapply fire cautery in curvature which is in a spasmodic nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When pains of joints are caused by moisture that is spread to each member of the body, and when pain comes on foot, which the physician calls "podagre" properly, and when it is from cold cause and cures of medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in such manner:
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	Make the mound of cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the olive oil cautery be according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you prick on the face of the foot, then make fire cautery at all the fire cautery that one calls a "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come just to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then make three or four cauteries on each knee, with all the olive oil cautery;
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	and if you have a more skillful hand, then do more, but do not hold your hand for too long, only as much as the thickness of the skin can be burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery that we described in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, then make points around the finger joints two lines;
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if it remains a point of pain in two places, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand;
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	and if the pains come just as cuts or just as swellings, cauterize each part, and make good governance for the patient and prepare medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make good government and you purge bad blood, he will be healthy with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the treatment of this face
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When a fracture comes from anger, and the veins descend to the ankle and it is new, then it is necessary that when you want to cure the vein, it does not harm that one day.
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and that he uses things that loosen the belly, so that the threads descend from his belly;
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and instruct him to hold his arm as long as the vein is repaired, and you reset it with your fingers, and mark from below the fracture on the bone of the thumb, and at all one sign that is similar to half a circle above the body;
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then heat the cautery to the form that it is
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is clear and it casts off unhealthy things.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then reset the bulbs to their place;
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and the ministers hold their hand on it so that they do not return backwards;
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	and work well the thighs of the patient, and put beneath him a cushion and a sheet on the thighs, and another on the foot which holds his hands;
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	then put the cautery on the sign at all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it as long as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, then recommence again another time until you reach just to the bone;
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and take care subtly that the bulb does not slip when you perform the cautery;
que tu ne le brulasses;	so that you do not burn it;
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and so that the patient does not die, or another evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And you know that when you do not approach the bone with the cautery, your operations are worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is necessary that the cauterers of children be subtle according to the measure of their years, and of great men also great according to their measure.
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	after three days, heal the limb with a gentle cauterization so that the numbness is lifted;
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	after healing other limbs so that it is healthy, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days until the wound is well cicatrized;
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	and it is necessary that his bandages be loosened for a long time, so that the boils do not burst when he gets up to go to his chamber.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, have a well-made crutch presented to him, and use it for 40 other days.
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and let him have good rest, so that he works little and guards against too great a replenishment of drinking and eating, and of too high a temperature.
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	and when he makes this instruction, he will be entirely healthy.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will tell about the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When roots grow into other abdomens and are conjoined, and you see that they do not grow further, then have the fire cautery made according to their quantity, and be careful with the third heat of heart.
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the treatment according to what we have said;
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the ancients have said that one should be cauterized with the cautery at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the level of the inch and make a line according to the width above the wound, and another below, and hold your hand in all the cauterized claw-like [instrument].
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and more moderate.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in no member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to a member, whether from falling or striking, and that pain lasts a long time, and the treatment of medicine is of no value, then it is necessary for it to be cauterized with the cautery called "points", and let the cauteries be according to the length of the member and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of twisting and of its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	if he is healthy from the first cautery, it is good;
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	by this name, recommend another cautery on top of that, for it is customary that it should be moved to the nearest member, because it is necessary that you make the cauteries until the patient is healthy.
de meselerie	of messelry
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The massages are often aided by cautery with great help, and likewise the disease that comes from the putrefaction of flux and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	You cannot see that it should be cauterized, take heed because the disease is at the beginning, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and does not descend nor stay, and you doubt that the corruption will not spread throughout the entire patient, then make five cauteries on the chief.
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I am the new head towards the forehead at the end of the veins;
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and it is behind the two horns, and it derives from the little hammer;
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and it leaves so much in your hand that the cauteries come right up to the bone, and as much as the crusts burst forth if the vapors of the great humors can issue forth;
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the mixture is scattered everywhere;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and it appears manifestly, if it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries that we have said or head, and one cauterizes on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one on the chest and another on the sides, and two on the shoulders;
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and it is on the joints, and it is on the tender flesh, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands;
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and be careful with the nerves that are on the last layer of skin calculating, so you do not burn them;
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and never make a cauterization on the bone of the thumb, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And know that the more you do cauterization, the more it does harm, and it hurts instead of helping;
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	and know that the patient feels no pain from the cauterization if it is done as the healthy person would feel it, because the body is already almost entirely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of the iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterwards, treat the wound with flour dust several times with honey and other treatments until it is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When swelling comes into a member and is treated with medicines and oils and plasters, and it does not heal, then you should make cauterizations on the member according to the size and smallness of the member;
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	and let the cautery be a little inserted between the skin of the arm;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the wounds so that they are healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And often one performs cautery on the hand and foot and back, at the outlet of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus if it is relieved of the inflammation;
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	and in no way should one interfere with it unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the outlets of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	about ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the disease called "albaras" is enveloped, and the engines of medicine are of no value, then cauterize with a cautery a little deeply, according to the quantity of the skin of the arm, until the whiteness is relieved, and its color is changed.
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	then heal with flour of veatches and of lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of the colon and blood of the almond tree, each a part.
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be entirely wrapped together, and let it be tied with a bandage, and let it be elevated to the level where it will be healthy.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a cancer appears at the beginning, and you want to stop it, if you cauterize with a cautery that resembles a circle, entirely around the tumor.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And always the wise men say that one should perform cauterization also at the middle of the channel of the sore;
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	and always it does not seem to me good, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already wanted to avoid it happening anytime;
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	and more rightfully it is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circle", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot heal
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays healing or because of the superfluity that it does or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has little blood, or because of the tension;
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you hasten to amputate:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then you cauterize around the area of small pricks, pricking;
aprés le laisse ensi.	afterwards let it be so.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it hastens to worsen.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you want to pierce all around the cautery, then heat the cautery of copper, which is its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this illness called "adubelati" so that the cauteries have pierced the heart, and be such the cauteries that the patient feels relief in some manner that the course of the disease is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards, treat until it is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment of fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another kind of illness there is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a withering of the members, for it withers the members just as the rust consumes the dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this disease in the patient who can suffer from cauterization together with fire, then heat up the small and large cauters gently, according to what is suitable for the patient or where the disease is.
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	afterwards cauterize all parts so that you extract all the corruption, and none of it remains, so that everything which is corrupted may be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then let it be for three days, and put on the cauterized places a soothing balm made with oil as long as the burning of the fire is removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of swollen limbs producing flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it's good.
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	and if not, then recommence the cauterization on what remains of the corrupted limbs.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this mangy condition was never cured by medicine except in the case of fire cauterization.
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	but every way fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the treatment of the ague medicine in the division:
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	take the quantity that you have in hand.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	for pores that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often it happens that the feet are paralyzed by a weakness which is called "cold" according to our intention, and it is a large faulty swelling that affects the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterizations of this disease are in two manners.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is to know fire cauterization and hot water cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Fire cautery is that you heat I heated cautery as if it were a hollow pen, and make it from good iron to the measure that it can hold the nail on all sides, and that it has subtle margins;
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	after heating everything hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it comes to the source of the nail;
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and let it stay thus for three days until it begins to make a purulent discharge;
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	then make a plaster of wild savages' herbs boiled with oil, and let the plaster stay on all night, and the nail will fall out and be disrooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound of burning by anointing so much that it be sound.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are turned around by defective limbs, and many times it happens in the hands and in the feet, then it is necessary that you apply cauterization of warm water;
et est en teil maniere:	and it is in such a manner:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	take a cane of iron or of steel, or a pointed instrument, and place it on the nail and the ankle, that is to say for removing warts;
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	and place the cane on it so that it presses all around, then I put a little warm water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the cane reaches to the root of the nail, and thus find the warm water way deep into the root;
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	and let the patient suffer a little the biting of the warm water for an hour;
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	then leave it thus, and it will uproot everything to its very roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus you do one after another, as long as you stretch those who are in the body, then heal the wounds that cause shame.
li cure dou trembler	the treatment for trembling hand
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When some shudder with cold or nerves, or from a four-day fever or another, if it is necessary that you apply three or four fire cauterizations on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra.
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and one on the foot, and one on the stomach for an olive-tree cautery;
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	if you leave the shuddering, and hasten the healing of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of pus-filled boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Several times they appear through skin defects, or pus-filled boils, which come from corrupted large masses.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	if it is necessary at first when they appear that one applies fire cauterization on each head of the pustule:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	a subtle fire cautery made from the wood of myrtle, so that the point is seized by the fire, or with the root of a long aristologe, or with a lentricular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And sometimes they cauterize at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow worse from then on, but are freed from the superfluities that come from them, and are healthy.
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times there occur great disturbances of blood in the artery that is connected to the wound that comes from the outer skin, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cauterization of a limb, and similar things;
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	and it is very grievous to staunch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And always when it happens to anyone, if you hasten to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it very tightly so that the blood is appeased beneath your finger, and does not issue forth anymore;
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	then apply to the fire the olive oil cauterizers, many small and large ones, as long as they are completely red;
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	then take I, or large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is located, and apply the cauterizer to that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cauterizer there until the blood is stanched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it happens that when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another of the cauteries that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not cease from doing one after the other as long as the wound is still inflamed;
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	and beware that you do not irritate the nerve which is affected, and that another evil does not come upon the patient;
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	and know that when the wound does not close over the artery, one cannot easily restrain it meantime as the artery is large, so it is not by one of the four methods that we have said:
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	either by cauterization, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong binding with a thread, or by medicines placed upon which have the power to restrain blood;
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	and be bound and restrained immediately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers the stanching of the bleeding wound tightly with strips or by placing heated things on it, or similar things, does not benefit if they do not do it little by little.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if it happens to no one and there is no better medicine present, then one must put their finger index on the wound of the vein as we have said, and bind well until it is restrained above the wound and above the vein;
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and do not move the finger, but the millet of the cold water should be very cold so that the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped.
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	and make an inquiry beforehand about those things which he has need of cauterizations and of medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book on surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have said in the first chapter that every disease in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire or with burning medicines, and the materials and causes and instruments and forms of cauterizations.
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and I have placed that chapter of the loins just below the feet, and I will proceed in this chapter by the same method by which one finds more lightly what one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first one of the cauteries, and because of this it requires more caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things;
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	Where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many sorts of people come to cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	if they come from such who aggravate their illness so that they die easily because of the weakness that they find in their disease, and the greatness of their evil.
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	and of these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And of these there is one who gives you his sense, and says:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am beware";
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the disease is despising.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but place greater caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not open foolishly but wisely of those things of which you are certain, and of which you can have taken and lost.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your ailments so that health may be converted to salvation;
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	and this will help you to acquire a good reputation, and glory, and memory of longevity.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Fathers give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you want to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have arranged this chapter in divisions, according to what is before or the chapter of cauteries, which I have divided from head to feet, because you will find it easier to master.
dou chief plein d’aigue	of a head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	Be aware that this illness comes very often to children at birth, and when the midwife holds the child's head too strongly;
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and it never comes from a cause that is known.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this illness except in children, and nearly all those whom I have seen hasten to death;
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	and therefore it seems to me that I should leave the work in part to other cures.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head grew so much each day that it could not support its own weight;
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and the moisture was so great that it caused death, and this moisture is gathered beneath the bone under the siphac, between the heart and the bone;
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and the operations are such that when moisture is between the heart and the bone, and abscesses are small, you make a large incision in the head.
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and let it be as long as two of us, so that the moisture flows;
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and see there the form of the spatula-shaped:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more increased, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the form of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs that you see are the sutures of the head overturned in each part, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not respond to you:
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	if it is necessary that you make three incisions in the head according to this method:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	Afterwards, hold the incisions with dressings and powders, and I put in wine and oil, and leave it thus until the fifth day;
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	then dislocate it, and treat the wound with tents and with ointments, and let the head be held steady, and give to the patient dry meat in moderation, little by little, until the member is comforted and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another way of incising is to examine where the greatness of the abscess opens, and the gathering of the water.
car aucune fois est elle devant;	for it is never in front;
aucune fois derrier;	never behind;
aucune fois en destre;	never to the right;
et aucune fois en senestre.	and never to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Cut then there where the abscess opens, and the gathering of the water, and you do it according to what you can about it;
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and beware that you do not cut the artery;
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and let flow a little blood, if the patient dies from the corruption of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of swelling
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens that a patient has a disease called "catarre" in the eyes or in the breast, and the disease is chronic, and the medical treatment does not help, then the last resort is cauterization with fire, which one copes with by burning the .ij. arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	It is necessary then, when you cut the veins, that the patient makes his head recoil;
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	after you rub the skin with a rough cloth so much that the arteries appear, then the patient stretches out his neck under the whole cloth;
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	Then look where the veins beat, and the veins of one and the other are behind the ears, and few are responded.
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then mark the veins of the enclosure, then cut one and the other with a sharp instrument of two edges, as long as the vein leads up to the bone, and it should be done by the width of the top of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, insert the pointed instrument beneath the artery and cauterize above, cutting also as .ij. two at the traverse.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cauterized, then the blood flows back up continuously afterwards.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not open to feeling, it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then mark the enclosure and cut up to the bone.
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	and it is necessary to put blood flow there if it is six inches, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the replenishment of the artery.
puis regarde la plaie:	Then look at the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	if it remains on the bone a little below the symbaphyphus, if you cut what produces abscesses here and there, then strain the wound and bind it, and the treatment of ointment until it is healthy.
de emigrainne	of the emigrant
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old emigrant comes, and has a catarrh, because of the moisture of the tears and the heat in the temples and the old worn-out forehead and similar things, and it is treated by ways of medicinal cures and all that does not profit him, if we extract the arteries of the temples and their cauterizations, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the method of extracting them is that the patient makes the hairs on their temples grow back, and pays attention to the artery that opens in the temple, for it opens well with its beating, and is hardly restored except in some homes where they are too cold.
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and if it is restored, then the patient stretches out their neck from some wraps, then rubs the area with a rough cloth, and raises the area of warm water so that the artery opens manifestly;
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	then take the spatula in the form of which it is here:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then pull it upwards with pincers, and separate well the membranes that are beneath each part;
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	and if the artery is subtle, turn it to the point of the anvil, then cover that part according to the quantity of the two hips.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For she is not cupped, if they do not jump the blood all at once.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And let flow three fluids from the sixth [degree of] heat, just up to the third;
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you ligate it in two layers of a strong double silk thread, which will not obstruct before the closure of the wound, and will stop the flowing of blood;
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	then remove the superfluity which is between the two ligatures at that hour, and then, if you see fit, if you cauterize with a cellular cautery up to the bone as long as the head is coped;
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and it is the moderate work, if the patient has no fever and he is of warm complexion.
