Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For the cauterizations are helpful in ending the moisture:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	because it is of greater aid against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Where it is necessary to extract the arteries that one fills the hole with much cotton and places well-made tents;
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and when you dislodge them, they must be treated with dry medicines that make flesh grow, and with tents, until they are healthy;
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	and without touching the artery so much as you can, if you hasten to cop the wound by cauterizing, or you fill the void with vitriol and hold it in your hand so the blood is staunchied;
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	and if you do not have this remedy, put your finger on the wound so that the blood is congealed, and raise the wound with cold water until the bleeding stops, and hold it steady as it is necessary;
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	and that which is more deadly and easier in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this trenchant cauterizing iron of two edges, but the trenchant edge should be well sharpened to avoid staying too long over the wound.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they hold less of their heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And you should have between the two cauteries a space of a thumb's width, and then when you have signed on both sides, and you measure the iron rod fiery hot until it comes just to the bone, and touches the vein on both sides.
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and they should be separated between the two heads because it is not possible to cauterize everything all at once.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and that is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	of the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes are flowing down due to veins that are on the top of the head from the fire, and it does not benefit from a cure by medicine that one makes, and you see the face of the patient becoming red, and feel at the forehead an abnormal gait as if from tremors.
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and the eyes are tired and moist so that the hair of the papers is fallen, and the papers are scorched, and burned by the heat of the tears, if you have need of this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And they call the old "contused cure", and it is that you make three incisions on the forehead of the patient who has this disease, with hairs growing from the front, then make three equal cuts according to the length of the forehead.
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and let one of the incisions be thus, like two dots on the forehead going downwards to the nose, and the others two on the sides near the papers, and beware of the incision of the arteries that are on the sides near the papers;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and align your hand with the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be the quantity of three fingers across the joints;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and much of cloth to suck out the blood, then apply the spatula acute at two parts where it is the shape;
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	of the incision that goes to the temple up to the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape off all the crust that is between the two fissures to the entire width of the syphac which is on the bone, then make another section of the mean incision just up to the other second, and then extract this spatula-like thing.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put in the first fissure the instrument that is called "cultellare", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is smooth, not very sharp, and that's its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge sloping towards the airy flesh of the heart, and the blunt edge towards the bone, and the joint as far as it reaches the middle wound.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	And cut off the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as far as the incision is continuous up to what opens on the bone, and then make another section in the mean fissure up to the other defect.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then extract the blood equally, and press out the bone for the blood taken.
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put on soaked cloths in wine and oil and in vinegar, and beware that apostemes do not develop there.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and on the third day, release the ligature, and I will show you a great remedy of hot water, then the treatment with royal balsam ointment with rose oil, and other treatments that one uses to cure wounds, until it is healthy.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyelids
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When a vein is inflamed from habitual abuse, and you see the eyes clouded and small, and dimming the sight, and blistered skin.
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hair falls out, and where the head is in the front of a painful ache, and the patient is exhausted;
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	then you know through these accidents that those matters and this cathartic do not come from many veins, and the mournful cure that it is, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you instruct the patient to shave their forehead, then make a great incision in the forehead, and another so large I do not dare.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin from the fissure of the left temple to the right temple, and so let the incision be just up to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and stretch out your hand near the roots of the temples that move to the brain;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is uncovered, suck up all the blood with a sponge, and then swab between the two lips of the fissure and put in much cotton, and tighten with a linen bandage;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	then apply warm dressings made of wine and oil, and beware of a sudden aposteme.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	when it is numb, it is necessary that you rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with exciting remedies that cause flesh to grow.
En teil maniere:	In such a manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of colofinum, and make an emplaster;
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and administer it to these wounds to grow flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the inflammation of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that falls into the ears is one of four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	either grains, or beast, or rock from the mine or similar things like iron.
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	or seeds, such as jasse, fava beans, peas;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or flowing things such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls in the pierced ear or another manner of thing that does not adjust to the ear, nor grows in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see a stone, distill some little droplet of violet oil or sesame oil, then it facilitates extraction;
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and make the condition stern, and stop up the nostrils when the sternness comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool;
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and stop up the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times relief comes through this treatment;
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not bring relief, then facilitate the extraction with subtle pinches, because that is the method:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If it brings relief through pinches, that's good;
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	if not, then facilitate the extraction with a subtle onion-like small doublure;
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	and if it does not bring relief through that, then make a pipe of copper and insert the head of the pipe into the ear or piercing hole strongly, and stop up what is around the pipe with wax so that air cannot enter with the pipe;
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	Then the fiery cauterization is formed, because many times it comes forth as we have said;
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	and if it does not come forth in this manner, then take glue from that and take the eyes, and put in some instrument which is at a point to make it, and put a little cotton around;
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	then press the glue onto the stone or whatever that may be, and cauterize strongly.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if it does not burst forth from all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut open the ear thus so that an abscess falls into a vein, and spasm;
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of the cutting is that you first make the patient sane from the cephalic disease, and extract some blood according to its virtue, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear where it depends on the fat or lean;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the wound be as crescent-shaped as a moon, until you reach the stone, then suck according to your power, and hastily bring it to your mouth;
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the treatment so that it be healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer an extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot exit, then administer the spatula with subtle thrust according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not do it when you think that the grain is moistened by the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces;
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract with subtle pincers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be alleviated.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water that falls into the ear, it is necessary that the patient use the sternuation of conditi first, and fill the ear with a lot of cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him sit on that shoulder where the ache is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	Let her walk for this, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	if not, take many pieces according to the length of your thumb, tender and light, and heat them a little at the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and put the patient a hole or perforation in their ear, and sew it with thread from another piece of skin, and attach it to another skin on the skin that is in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not cease from making this skin to skin as long as the water issues forth entirely, and thus it will be entirely free;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see, take the joint, and put one of the heads in the ear, and the other head is seized by fire until the most tender joint is burnt;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then remake another part of other joints until the water issues forth entirely, as we have said in the skin.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, as a flea and similar things, treat it thus as we have said in the division;
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is of large body that one can feel it, then prepare an extraction with pincers;
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and it is the thing most easy to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you cure them as we have said in the section and where you treat the distillations, and the cure does not profit, if it is necessary that you expose the ear to sunlight:
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	if they open no worms, if they draw them out as subtle pincers, and if they do not appear, take the cane of where it is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And insert the most subtle instrument in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then suck formally all the way to the cane;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	do this as often as all the worms are seen.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, stop up the cane with cotton as I have said in the stone;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not sweat as we have said, administer gentle distillations that the ancients have experienced in the treatment of wounds, and you will find them or treat with distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	and if you distill your oils and your medicines into the ear with all this instrument, because it is the method as you see;
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And whether of silver or copper tubes below at the small holes, and above them pour to distill;
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	and to press within the distillation to the copper instrument well-made for that, and if you see take the receiver and envelop it around the point where the cotton comes;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	then you pour your oil or your juice, and that which you take of your medicines in the reed, and the reed is in the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	then put everything into the receiver with all the cotton, and press your hand gently so that the oil is distilled or flows out of the ear;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and let the patient sense it internally, and so are the distillations; I heat them up with fire in this way, as one distills into the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the inflammation of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born who does not have some perforation in their ears;
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and this same thing happens to men through swelling of wounds, or of flesh born inside the ear, and these swellings come sometimes deep into the ear, if one cannot see them;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and sometimes it happens that I thoroughly clean out the perforation, and then I see it very well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which comes deep inside, if one cannot see it, is of grievous sanitation in many conditions, and in that case it is necessary that you place the ear of the patient in the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look within:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the apparent obstruction, if the work is entirely of this spatula-like material from which it is formed:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And let it be sharp and cutting on both sides all along, so that it does not numb the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the obstruction is of flesh born or growing from the ear, if you hold it with subtle pincers, and gently touch, until that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the suppurations are deeply rooted in the ear, take a subtle, light razor and heat it slightly by fire, then place it at the root of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the obstruction where the patient feels great pain in the ear, touch lightly, and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the perforation, and apply it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and apply it with red oil, and sprinkle on powdered glass powder.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear inflamed, it is necessary that you apply the tent and remove another infected tent made of rosed oil and wax, so that the inflammation may be removed;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if a flow of blood comes, soak an sponge and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that eliminate the flow of blood which are or treat with distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	These are the thorns that come from papers of eyes when they are moist and dry, if it is necessary that you extend them with tongs and pincers, and cut with a spatula of their roots;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put on the place a glassy ointment rubbed.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if without decay, so the cautery of subtle lenticular fire, and the cauteryizer after the incision is worth more;
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and many times they repair, since nothing remains of their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauteryized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the crust
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Often times there come in papers of the eyes certain things that appear rough in their form and hardness, and because of this, this disease is called "grandine", and it is a gathering of thick moisture above and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	The works are such:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	Take heed when the grandine moves from one part to another, and it's a light thing to know.
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Make the donor of the large wound, then lightly scrape each part, then take it with pincers, and cover.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you cannot cover it without piercing a little the skin, do not harm anything to the patient.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	And if the wound is large, sew it up with a suture, and treat it until it is healthy.
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	And if it is small, do not use force, for the joints will soon restore themselves and become strong again.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the vein is descending from the bottom of the ear towards the upper part, reverse the paper, and stretch the vein to a pinch, and press on one side and the other.
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is separated by incision, it does not hurt at all;
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the vein is pressed, lift the salty water with oil, and heal the place of those who are injured so much that the patient may be healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a fatness that is injured in the papers above, and this happens more to young children, and hurts much their eyes, and they come to cathars at dawn, and cannot gaze at the light of the sun because the tears hurry to their eyes;
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and for this they lie down on their faces immediately, and sleep on them, and their papers beneath their eyebrows are moist that the inflammation and appearance have covered over the exinach which opens in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press your hand against your fingers and feel the muscle tension between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the treatment is that the patient puts his head on a healthy side;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take the linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains excess of each part, then place it on him;
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your two hands on one side and the other, so that the excess is gathered within the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then make in the middle of the moisture a cutting spatula making a cut of a large width, and it should not be larger than the wound one makes when opening a vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and make the skin deep enough so that you reach the excess;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in many dispositions comes excess from the cut, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Remove then all at once a piece of torn cloth between your two fingers at the defect, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is spread out;
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	and beware that you do not thrust into the fissure, that you do not reach the entire spatula up to the eye, that you do not bruise it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if the instrument does not open at the beginning of the fissure, increase it a little bit so that the fissure opens more easily as it appears;
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	then extract it as we have said, then wrap in a clean cloth and in water, and put on the limb, and strain with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who break their own skin and put it on to corrupt the moisture that is retained.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal until it be healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there comes a hot abscess to the limb, then heal with emplasters soothing until it be healthy.
des poilz des papieres	the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When in papers (skin) unnatural hairs are thrust aside from their natural place, and are enveloped, they harm the eyes, and bring about kinds of diseases such as customary tears and softening of the skin and albumin, so much that it is the cause of destruction of the eyes.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	and it is the treatment in four ways:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	Here is the translation:
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you put the patient's head upright, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand.
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	if it is converted, it is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	see if not, if you push a needle all along the thread above;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let it be along the margin of the paper where the hairs grow from these hairs, and pull the thread above all the way to the paper, and turn it to the razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then make an incision below the paper, below the aligned hairs, all the way to the spatula-like instrument, from the large lancet up to the small;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then extract the thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and drapery, then sign on the paper a figure of an inch, like the leaf of myrtle, and however it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see elevated the paper which is divided into toes.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if you take a part which is mastered, one copes with a great quantity of the paper according to how much the paper is softened.
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then make a whole spatula on the two lines that you have signed, and start from the great large lancet just up to small;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let it be one of the incisions near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the onion in one of the two angles of the horn, then scrape everything;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then assemble the two lips at a seam of a needle with all the subtle thread of flax, and suck out the blood, and make a bond of the superfluity of the threads on the two eyebrows at all kinds of gluey things, if you want to do this;
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if it doesn't work, if you don't have a cure, then leave the seam and the threads until three or four days;
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then cure the wound without tight constricting things, for the skin revives at the suddenness of the wound and its assembly, but the constricting is murderous (as the ancients said), and it's work without fear;
et si a une autre maniere:	and if in another manner:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and it is that you shape the skin into a figure like the leaf of myrtle, as we have related, at three ounces of ointment according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply this to those who have small equal forces in harmony with the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you cannot hold the bandages, and the thing is not even, take a needle or it has one thread, and put it in the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and put another thread from the large larder, and the second thread from the small one, and assemble between your two threads evenly;
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin upon which you have signed, as we have related, then assemble the two lips of the wound by constricting, and cure until it is healthy;
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with a gentle and similar soothing application;
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and often it happens that the hairs of the parchment are converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	if it is necessary, you should use what we have said about incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of wounds is according to this form:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and it is that you should convert the parchment and make them inside according to what I have said, and then make two wounds by art, and two subtle threads as long as the parchment and the width of the spatula-like instrument is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and cut as two heads of two parts or where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble one and the other subtly above what overhangs from the parchment of the eye, and pull out the two wounds of the two parts forcibly;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and let it thus for some days, and the skin that is constricted will become numb and weak, and porous, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it delays, if the scalp adheres to the bone, then cure it until it is healthy;
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	and when the wound is sewn, and if the paper is lifted, and they will no longer puncture the hair;
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	and it is the shape of the two canals that you will make according to this design, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	the operations are such that you take a subtle needle, and insert a soft and subtle silk thread;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	then assemble the heads and tie one to the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm's width long;
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	then order in the hunt another subtle thread of briefly twisted silk, and tie the two heads of thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then put the patient's head in your healthy one;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and let it be under the sun so that the work is clarified, for this is a subtle and minor work, then put the needle at the root of the hair that is affected, and make it pierce the papyrus hastily until you draw it above the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	then extract the hair up to the root, and put into the root that hair, if there is one or two or three or more;
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	then extract your hand so that the hairs come out from the root into the papyrus with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the root is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the root down to the bottom of the thread that you had ordained there, so that the root comes out from the hole above and you see it by the sight of the eye;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then you should pull out the splint and the thread, and close the eye and let it close for two or three days, until the hair grows back into its place and the flesh grows over it.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	and if the hairs are short, accompany the long hair of the natural whiskers, and be lifted with that which you let it be, until it is elongated and then set free.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the burning of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease called "aleacrati" or the pus comes into the eye, if there are two manners of it:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from a cut, or from cauterization, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the manner of operating on it is that you open the suture, and separate the lips of it, and put in threads of linen, and leave it until it is healthy;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and it is not suitable that you use in the treatment of it things that dry and restrain.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	Because you do this, if the illness returns worse than the first.
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but I observe things that are soothing, like fenugrec.
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the rose-water or ague, and flaxseed, being cooked, and anointments of dyaquilon founded on none of the oils, and I enveloped a tent, and the cure of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your cure is that you take heed that it does not sink according to the form it had before.
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these works that we have said are not stronger than the treatments of this illness, so it does not relapse according to the form it had before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is beneath, which truly is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	and the way of the operation is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and prick the flesh, and make it pierce from the left arm to the right, so that the threads come together at the head of the flesh;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then the flesh is above all the bristle, and the scalpel has a large spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the skin returns according to what it should be, that's good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if not, then take the rasp and put it in the crack, and turn the skin, and make two cracks or sew up inside the skin;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the heads of the two cracks at the two angles of the incision that you have cut, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is just like the shape of a letter which has not "I griesche";
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then remove that flesh, according to the quantity whose edges are thus arranged beneath, of what follows the skin, then adjust the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of flax;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the treatment of what we have said about softening medicines, and of tents, until it is healthy.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the illness comes from a crack or a stitch or a cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain crack underneath the hairs of the papers, and according to what is presented here.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then dissect between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said;
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters appear to engineer everything so that they can make it return to its natural shape;
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the same patients, according to what they need in terms of work and instruments in various arrangements.
dou soudement de la papiere	You burn with the application of paper.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this joint has stuck together in such a way that the paper on top is glued with the white of the egg, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it is necessary to put the point of a razor underneath the paper, and lift it up high.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and hold the pincers, as long as you cut what is attached to the subtle spatula, which should not be too pointed nor too cutting, so that the patient cannot suffer that the spatula is too pointed and does not blister the eye;
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and let your incision be, where you carefully strip away the assembled one, lightly, so that the skin regains its natural shape;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and it is healthy throughout the assembled one, and never irritates the sharp salty eye, and raises the sweet water, and the collarbone;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then put between the skin and the eye a linen bandage, and place on the eye a moistened flaxen cloth in abundance of egg whites;
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after three days, use sweet collars and similar things as long as it is healthy.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	Know that the nail is according to two manners:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	It is nervous and resembles ivory, and another that is not nervous but resembles white congealed moisture, which when touched by iron and pressed by the pincers, it cannot be moved.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	and one and the other resemble the great artery, and grows little by little until it covers all vision and all light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his head in a healthy position, then he opens his eyes.
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lifts the skin with your hand, then bends the finger into small doubles, and holds it above;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and insert the hair of a horse, or of a calf, or of an ox, and pull it strongly.
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a little and fix it in the finger, and pass it through the entire needle, and tie the finger with a thread and hold it above, and strip all the hair from the side of the finger which joins the vein and the artery at the head, then cut the remaining part into the root of the artery with subtle and small forces, and let the natural flesh or artery, so that by the incision, the body of the veins does not become accustomed.
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and many times the nail is pierced at the ankle only, and at the thread, as we have said;
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then the scab forms a whole spatula full of pus where it is in its form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And take care that the spatula does not touch the raw flesh and break it, and that the prune is not pierced;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision, pour into the oil a little of bruised sage, and make a poultice from litharge, and leave it until the next day;
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal those things which he needs as long as it takes to be healthy.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push in the needle, and the ankle joints cannot enter, many times this type of nail is cured by medications;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and grow thus as I have told in the division, and if you see it covered, then open the oil of the patient, and take the lighter spatula a little gently according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	And you raise the nail subtly, and if you see that it diminishes at no point and the reason is pressed, then distill from your mouth into the hollow colier made of litharge and red colier, and wipe the eye just to the other hour;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then recommend the other treatment according to this same work, until it is completely restored.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the wound, as an abscess grows, then lance it, and first cure the hot abscess so that it may be healthy, then recommence the work as before, so that it may be healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the skin is painful from the tears at night in the eye by great annoyance, then suspend it on the onion, and cover one part and not entirely, so that tears do not come there;
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	then distill into the hollow red colier made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the nail
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	The eyes of some men never saw the red flesh, and uncover the plumule and hold steady on the papyrus and turn to the deformed, and resemble a rose of balusters;
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the operations are such that the patient puts his head in a healthy position, then he opens his eyes, and collects all that flesh as convenient signs to this, and holds it with strength;
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	then grasp the first flesh, and take all grasping to the healer just until the end, and beware that you do not blink an eye during the operation;
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision be a gentle spatula which we have said in the incision of the ankle and with small forces because one breaks the sebum, thus like the form afterwards this chapter demonstrates;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is accomplished and all the flesh is broken, then apply the oil of broiet or you distill red coliere and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the eye a piece of cotton with water of eggs, so that it be assured against hot aposteme;
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if he delays nothing, and the blood flows back up, and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the abscess with soothing things that reduce the hot abscess;
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work as soon as he is healthy, and thus make sure that the flesh is adjusted in the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But always it is necessary that you adjust the treatment of each weak eye according to the natural way;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and from the accidental way, in work of iron;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand into any of these works as long as you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	There are certain red veins that are covered on the eye, and they obstruct the vision with their work and totally blind the eye sometimes.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	It is necessary therefore at first that you examine the eye, in which it is, it is false, and there is no other illness besides the cataract.
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then operates on it in such a manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Instruct the patient to place his head in a healthy position, then suspend those veins all around the anointed area according to his wisdom, and let the anointed areas be subtle and doubly so according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be of one circle by degrees in the body according to this form.
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then one coils the veins subtly, and drains the blood hourly after another, until you see the removal of the veins that are farthest from the eye.
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and beware that you do not blind the eye at the points of the spatumiles, and perform this work at midday in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not omit more than those veins.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and when you have done this, then distill into the eye a green and red color to corrupt what is morbidly swollen below.

et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then apply the oil of iris, and heal the limb of dry things as long as it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times a swelling appears on the gums which the old people call "albulus";
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	it is necessary that you hold it back with bandages, and cut to its root, and let the blood or fluid flow;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then apply on the limb a glassy paste, or other powders that restrain and dry;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that which returns after the incision, and many times happens, then cut a second time, and cauterize:
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return again after the cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	the filthy ones
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they gather at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and often the teeth turn black and yellowish and decayed, so that the rot reaches the gums, and are the foul-smelling teeth;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	it is necessary that you seat the patient between your hands, and their head be in your lap, and take out the teeth or the scabs that appear, so that nothing remains;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and thus make of the blackness and the greenish color, and of the yellowness and other stains, so that they be eradicated;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if one removes what is at the first root, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, then start again from the second day and the third, until you have everything removed;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and know that teeth have need of various forms of instruments for extraction, according to what the work demonstrates, because the roots that one extracts from the teeth have other forms than those that one extracts between the teeth;
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others are prepared with you equipped.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of his pain that you delay to treat as much as you can, for this must not be done in a hurry.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a very high substance just up to then so that one has no excuse to rush.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained from treating, it is necessary that you are certain of the tooth that hurts.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and believes it is in a healthy tooth, and makes the good tooth decay.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and never does the pain depart from him for that, as much as the bad one is extracted, because we have already wanted to do it to these healthy ones.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth on every side, strongly to guard the gum from all parts.
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then place your fingers or subtle pincers at the first little by little, so that it is well loosened, then firmly fix the pincers.
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the head of the patient be stable between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and gently insert it into each part lightly, and remove it as you did previously.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the teeth are broken and worn away, it is necessary that you fill them with cloths, there where the holes are.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if you hold it subtly at the roots, so that it does not break while holding.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and it is necessary to work very carefully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you do well to be wary that you do not break it, and leave a part remaining, and reattach to the patient through the evil of the root, which causes greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And beware that you do not act like the ignorant surgeon, who through their haste and hardness often break the instrument, and do not amend what we have related.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but often come instead through the examination of this great disease for the roots that they remove, or for the instrument that they break, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is decayed, if you wash the affected area with wine or with vinegar and with saliva;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and we stop the flow of blood that comes, which often happens, if you apply the area with powdered vitriol;
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	and if it does not help, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The forms of instruments, where one must extract the teeth first, should be long and pointed and have large handles, so they do not slip when you pull the tooth;
et ce sont les formes:	and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of large limbs so that they do not bend in the shaft, and they should be of well-made iron, and they should be held by muscles to keep steady.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in the pulling, it is necessary that you place on the affected area cotton soaked in bitter wine I or II, as long as the gums are numb, then you apply the clamps called "algefri", from which the head seems to be like a beak of a swan;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and let them be made thus like a file and it is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with these tongs, then you must uncover the flesh entirely around the root, and apply the instrument called "althali", that is to say a scalpel, of which this is the shape.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break easily, and if its root goes up through this, it is good;
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	if not, then help with all the instruments, because of which the forms come here afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has many grooves, from which comes the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools that are before in the arrangement of the teeth, and of this instrument that resembles large forceps, from which comes the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let these instruments be strong so that they cannot break, and know that many of these dense instruments are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise masters subtly find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, because there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument for the diversity of wounds; and it does not break at all in the cartilage or in other bones, or it becomes porous, if they seek those instruments that they need, which I have told you, and help with the gestures, from which this form is:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let it be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, so it does not slip, but then it can hold and ostrute;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore to the bone the suitable medications, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, then take all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural course, and its shape is ugly, and especially in women with small mouths, then it is necessary that you know if the teeth are not born after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and one cannot make them straight or file:
adonques lou raie;	then the root;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is attached with the tooth, then take this instrument which has the shape, and is similar to a small beak, and let it be of iron pointed in a hook:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the instrument takes a little and little in the jaws for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, thus take the file of one part file as it is the form.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the file with which one makes the needles;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and apply a gentle touch with thumb and finger slowly, so they do not move until it takes hold;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then apply a gentle pressure at the end without any raspiness, and if the teeth are too sharp and it bites the tongue, you must file the asperity until it is even, so it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth aches
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front teeth are locked, whether by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on them so they chew, and you treat them with constricting medications, and that does not work;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	you must restrain it with a golden thread, for the silver wire turns green and rotten, but the gold does not move at all;
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thin thread be not too large nor too small, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you want to realign the teeth, take the thread and double strand between the two healthy teeth, then place the heads between the bad teeth, if there is one or more, until you feel strongly just up to the healthy tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then recommence the covering just up to the part where you started, and hold your hand subtly and strongly, until it does not move at all;
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then seize the heads of the thread with pincers, and assemble them, and put them between the healthy tooth, and place it so that it does not touch the tongue;
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	and then leave it thus tightly as long as it can stay, and if it comes loose, or the threads break, hold it with another thread;
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it stays and serves thus all its tension, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the adjustment of the two healthy teeth, and of the two jaws, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth falls out, if you reset it in its place, little by little, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and do not interfere with it, for one is not skilled and suffers, and never makes the shape of a tooth of ivory, and puts it in its place where the defect is, and holds it steady as we have said, and it stays and serves thus long tension.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of burning the ligature of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Never is it a natural bond that comes from under the tongue or naturally, which grows thus;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accidental wound soothing;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and hold their head in your healthy one, and lift the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	Then cut the nervous cord as wide, so that the tongue is dislocated from its holding, and if there is hardness or numbness, and it's a sudden injury, if you cut the uncinate and cut wide the cord.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and beware that the wound does not go too deep in front, because of the artery which is underneath;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done it, lift the lever of hot water and of hay, or of cold water, then put underneath the tongue a tent of linen;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and touch the patient's gum every night, so that the jaws cannot close.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if a flow of blood comes, then put on the lever a glassy powdered vitriol;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the wound does not heal, then cauterize it with a slow-cautery, which is good for that;
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then the treatment of another treatment until he is healthy,
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see a flesh-colored or black or hard spot, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is cancer;
