et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is due to the spleen, then make it on the right, and it is not necessary that the patient's gaze falls upon the incision, lest the superfluous fluids run to that weak spot;
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and the swelling, and lift your hand to the entire spatium between the skin and the fascia, just as in scraping out the quantity of an ounce or an eighth;
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Then prick the sharp point as far as the spatula comes to the empty space, and it is the level of the water, then draw it back, and it pushes this instrument from which it is the shape.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it resembles a subtle silver tube, and it is of copper or lighter arching, and has a small hole at the bottom.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and where it is shaped on one side, three holes;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two on another side, and one on the other;
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and it is the head cut like a pen, and it is the shape of the incision where the writers sharpen the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at the top above is the scalpel, so that when the instruments come to the water, they descend now onto the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	empty it then by half or a third part, because if you empty more than it needs at that hour, perhaps the patient will die from the relaxation of his spirit of the arm, or he falls into a swoon, or he approaches death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but according to the quantity of its strength, and according to what the dispositions of the strength of the patient signify, and his pulses;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then draw the instrument and hold the water, and it is held back now by the heart which stops up the passage that is on the skin, of which I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then reinsert the instrument the other way, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw water in a small quantity;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do it no way, and guard yourself from flowing too much but only a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt on the patient, and you leave much water, if the treatment of the grave or sandy heat, and by very sweet or bath and in the sun, and abstain from drinking.
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and the care of drying medicines as long as it is healthy, and to cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the rod
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No time is born a child who does not have holes in the penis, or the hole is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If you want to pierce them so that they do not have to perceive everything in the very subtle spatium, according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then put or pierce with a subtle instrument, and tie it up and hold it thus for three days or four, and when he wants to make urine, let the closure be opened, and make him urinate, and then replace it.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	and by chance, you will not find a problem, because the urine that comes forth does not let it close.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	The place where the perforation is small, if it is medicated with a thick cloth of wool, as we have said, so it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the penis in their place are blighted, because none are born with the penis at the head of the rod, because they cannot urinate before they lift their rod up high.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and they cannot ejaculate because the material cannot come up to the marrow, and it is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the operation is that the patient lies on their back, then the head of the rod and the handle are equally sized like the width of a penny, so that the perforating instrument is in the middle, as it should be.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and beware of the flow of blood that comes often, and if it happens, then stop what is bleeding blood, and heal the wound until it is healthy.
des pustules de la verge	blisters of the penis

de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not a dislocation of continuity as with other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	In every way when we make this work of our will, and properly with children, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the lightest for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not circumcise their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen the greatest part of my masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around the thigh, and with force, and all at once;
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	if the skin is cut because there are two layers, and by chance if one cuts on that above and delays that below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	Then the wound closes over, and the pain is double, and in the healing which is two days hence it is not assured of the point of the limb;
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and in the healing of the ankle by chance the iron slips, and corrodes the work, and many times it grows so that they have no need of healing and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the mending which is done with forces all the way to the thread of wire I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	Because when you press your hand, if you cut equally throughout, you feel it all tense;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but the thread should be well stretched around the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and the manner of the first operation is such that you make the child think, if it understands, that you do not force it to tie the thread around the penis too tightly, and then you make it move in all the ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then you make it stand between your hands straight, and hold the forces between your hands or below your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments;
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	then put your hand on the penis and blow or touch, and pull it up as high as the head of the penis is in;
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	then clean well the ordure that is assembled there, then tie it with a double thread, then tie it below one pox to another ligament;
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and you will hold it by the second finger on the pouch and on the index finger, and grasp between the two ligaments, then lift the cortex above hastily and draw the head of the rod;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow little by little, for that is the remedy;
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on it and on the powder I drizzle glue made from a half-cooked egg white, mixed with rose oil, good and fresh, and let it stay until the next day, and treat with another treatment until he is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The shape of the bandages for the mundification is this:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two heads should be tender and piercing, and the heads should be as large as the equal joint of the hand:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The mistake in the mundification is when the heart within goes to the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	then it is necessary that you stretch out to your finger, thus so that the humors make an abscess;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and equal balance, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, so hold it with a bandage, and then balance it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they surpass three days, and that which is beneath the rod is inflamed, so let it be until the abscesses are appeased, and scrape off lightly;
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	if you balance it as you can move, and guard against the part of the rod, it will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Heal then the limb of sudden wounds with powder, which we have said or treatise on powders, and if you balance double the measure of the outer, and it goes above, it will not harm at all.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Heal then, as we have said, until it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	due to retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is from obstruction of the kidney, or of congealed blood, or of a blow, or of a new wound, or of similar things, which we have spoken of in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine does not flow, and you see that the retention is due to the kidney which is hurt or compressed at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent over his knees;
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and they should place their feet on the back, and stretch out their belly from the upper part above the back, and the patient should strain to relieve himself as much as he can;
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then the neck of the bladder is constricted at the expression of the kidney above, because of which the urine flows;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer an extraction with all the instruments which are called "syringe", of which this is the form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and let it be of subtle silver threads light as a bird's feather;
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and let it be the length of a palm and a half, and subtly at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the method of extracting the urine is that you take a double thread, and tie it to the head with a piece of wool or cotton, and insert the head of the thread into the syringe;
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and cut the excess of the wool and insert it just at the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a seat, and raise the bladder and the rod with moist olive oil and water;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then gently insert the syringe into the rod, until it reaches the root of the rod, then bend the rod downwards towards the bowel;
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then apply the syringe before it reaches the bladder, and the patient feels it reaching the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order because of that which conducts or leads it astray.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then stretch the thread to the entire lane little by little, and the urine follows the lane, then it strays outside, and makes the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and continue with the syringe until the bladder is empty, and relieve the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the vein
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blood or pus comes into the vein, where putrefaction is assembled, and you have seen to distill sharp points and medicines, if you make all the instrument called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if it has three punctures:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	Two on one side, and one on the other, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the veins are chosen because the short medicine is such that it stops well the erect penis without addition, if one can then draw out the moisture, and apply as much as necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	and when you see that your medicines are in the bladder, put the head of the syringe into the moisture, and pull out the treating instrument which is inside;
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	If you draw moisture to the joint, and then strongly rebend the drawing thread;
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	if you enter the moisture there, and it will come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and it is the subtle form of the catheter by which one catheterizes the bladder:
si est ci:	if it is so:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is of silver or of copper, and it is the head higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and below at the seat or the chains fall;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture in it that you want to catheterize the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts in the form of a twisted double thread, and heat that moisture over the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then put the head of the catheter in the rod, then hold your hand on the bladder with all the moisture coming at once, until the patient feels that this moisture has just arrived at the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle on it, and pierce it around entirely.
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then insert the strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a beam, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument;
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do as if you had done with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have previously stated in the division the methods of piercing, and the extraction of assembled medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and we have said the difference between the piercing in January as reins, and all the signs, and in what piercing one should operate by size;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the rod;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is in the bladder if it often happens to children, and it's a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similarly to water in its subtlety;
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and it appears here and there, and rubs the patient's rod, and it bites many times, and then becomes stiff;
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and at much of these jumps the foundations;
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and it is easy the healing of children until they are four years old, and it is much grievous in old people, and it is as gentle moisture, to those who are between youth and old age;
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and it is the cure easier for those who have a large stone, than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to clean the patient with a clyster, in order to expel all the bad humors that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders one from questioning the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the feet, and make them lean forward and move downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and jumps out several times from the high place;
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	then have him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands are beneath his thighs, so that the vessel is entirely declining downward;
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	then the vein and touch inside;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not fall to the toucher of the whole, then anoint your right index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is old, or your left finger, if the patient is young and accomplished;
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and thrust it into its foundation, and touch the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, then anoint the neck of the vessel;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press on with your finger, and thrust it to the depth where you want to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the minister to press the vessel with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand above the loins, and with his left hand hold the skin which is beneath the loins in the part where the cutting is done;
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then I apply the spatula, which is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And make an incision between what is between the hip and the perineum, not in the middle but at the side of the left thigh;
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	and be straight on the stone, and the two should be equally or at the foundation, and the cut of the traversing tree should be wide enough to pass through, and within it is narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	by chance the press if the two that are at the foundation, so that they burst forth without effort;
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and know that there is a part of the stone where it has angles and margins:
si est griés a issir;	if it is difficult to remove;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is a part that is underneath, similar to a pebble, and rounded, whose removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	Where there are angles and margins, make the cut larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not jump, then you must stretch on the tendons which are like a thread at the head of the bone, to strongly stretch the stone so that it doesn't escape;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	where you apply underneath the subtle curved instrument at the head;
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot engineer it thus, then enlarge the small hole, and if the sense is disturbed, then stretch with vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	and if there is more than one stone, then apply the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then pull it out forcibly, and the small ones afterwards if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it needs to be operated on, and to make a bigger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For these things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	where he dies, or the urine comes back immediately because the bladder cannot hold it;
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but you must exert yourself to treat, or to remove the tendons, so much that you treat them by pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, apply the plaster of incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it in place, and put it on with a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or with oil and warm rose water and cold froid water, to soothe the hot abscess;
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	then restore the patient to their bed, and do not dislodge the bandage just until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, rub very well the joint with oil and water, then apply the ointment of diyafinicon and ointment of basilicon, until it is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if hot abscesses come in the wound and corrode, and congealments of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by that which holds back the urine, which is known in such a way that without passing with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	put forth your finger in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains there, it will corrode the bladder, and putrefy;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift the wound of water and of oil and of serum, and aid it in all the ways that you know, so that it may be healthy.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	and it is necessary that all the openings that you cure, that you tie the two thighs, and assemble the medicines on the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is conducted by the rod, and fixed in, and the urine cannot issue;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if the cure of what I say thus, that you often cut away, is an excuse for the cutting away by this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proved it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a rod of iron in this form and it is fixed at three angles in the thigh.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	then take the thread and tie it around the rod beneath the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then push the iron into the rod gently, until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the iron in your hand on the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side;
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	If the urine comes immediately, then press your hand on what is remaining of the stone which is within the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it is immediately broken, and jumps out with the urine, and the patient is cured;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do this because of anything that is defective, if you fill the space beneath the stone and another above, then make the penis in the place of the stone between the two ligaments, then extract it out, and release the ligament, and clear away the congealed blood that is in the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until he is healthy.
de la piere des femmes	of the stones of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It rarely happens that a stone is in the genitals of women, and if it happens at all, the treatment is grievous, and is defended against by three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman well acquainted who uncovers her mirrors, especially when she is pregnant.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well acquainted in this hand craft;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth manner is that the skin of the woman is more in the forefront than the skin of the man, because it conceals doing deeper cutting, and there is great fear. And if you need to sew it up, then you must take a wise woman well acquainted, and prick the place on, and if you don't find one, at least ask for a subtle mirror.
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and the present is a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the craft, and she instructs that she do what you command her to do from the examination of the skin;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look very well if the woman is a virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is necessary to thrust his finger or foundation and seek the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if it is found, if it is stuck under his finger, and recommend that she thrusts her finger or with the patient, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it gently from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then feel on the stone at the root of the thigh against the soft flesh, there where it is most apparent, and feel the stone in that part;
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move her finger on the stone or below, and let it be cut at the first small size;
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	then thrust the razor in the incision, if you feel the stone if it increases the wound so that the stone can be extracted further, and know that there are many kinds of stones:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	It is to know, small and large and thin and swollen, long and round, and which have roots.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	you examine the symptoms to know the issue.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if the wound does not heal, then apply to the vivid broth a poultice, and hold it in place for an hour until the wound is cleansed.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, until the stone is broken, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of the stone as tools for you to help in your operation.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if the wound does not heal, and it is of the artery that is cut, then apply powder on the wound and hold with tourniquets and bandages, and do not restart this, and leave the stone alone and do not touch it, lest by chance the patient may die.
puis cure la plaie.	then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the veins are purified, then return to your work, until the stone is loose.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Rheum is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white flux, which is beneath the skin of the loins, that contains the egg.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly on the web of the egg, if one believes that it is another eye;
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it's the skin of the conjoined twin between the white "syfac" that we have mentioned;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and they did not have a small pouch.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this limb is from weakness that comes to the joints, and it spreads that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And sometimes it comes from a blow on the joints, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	where it is declining into a yellowish color, or it's without red, or black, or watery pale, and this happens more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs of recognizing this assembly, for if it is or white "syfac" that we have mentioned, then it's the swollen abscesses, a little long as the figure of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around.

et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white membrane, then it feels very good;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	then when you want to know the color of the moisture, it is tested by the entire introspection, because its form is thus before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the inner quarter, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we cure with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his power and the replenishment of his body;

puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then prick the swollen siphac plain with a large perforator, and extract all the water, and then put your onguines, and it is the siphac above;
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the core of the joints, but only the siphac suffers;
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	take all or in pieces the subtle part of his costal, that if you do not take it very wisely, the water will return;
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the egg (vein) bursts for a tonsil, if you reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the siphac;
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then assemble the two leaves of the core of the joints to a crust, then cure it as with other wounds, until it is healthy.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you find the vein corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you ligate the vessels that are suspended, doubting the decay of blood.
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	Then cauterize the entire affected area, and extract the humor, and treat it as we have said.

si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	then cauterize the other part just as you did the first alignment, then suck out the blood, and put into the wound a soft linen cloth anointed with rose oil;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put on top another soft linen cloth soaked in wine and oil, and put over the two joints, and put above double layers of cloth, and bind it all together with a bandage that is according to this form;
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths, and fill them with linen fragments according to this likeness, and assemble them by sewing along the throat of the arms, and one of the heads takes hold at the base just up to the back, and the other at the part of the thigh;
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two fingers on the two angels, and let the entire assembly of the restraint be in the loop of the arm;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and no time is it medicated with this remedy of cautery in the size of iron, and it is that you grasp the subtle cautery scalpel, and cut the skin of the thighs, and be heated as we have said, so that the white syphilis which contains the water is discovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if you take the cautery in this form, and pierce that syphilis as onyx, and burn it with this subtle cautery hot iron:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And cut in all the ways that you can, until you extract everything;
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and be careful that the iron does not touch the egg;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and know that this work is more salvatory;

et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if there is no thing that does against you, whether an abscess or a break in the blood or something else, if you cure what does against you, according to what has been said before.

de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the treatment of this disease there is fear in many dispositions, because it seems to me that few are worth leaving;
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you about the work and the appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say therefore that many abscesses come to a crisis, and meanwhile are like boils;
et c’est par mout de cas.	and it is in most cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to know by excessive inflammation and fever, which spreads to the joints, or from a blow;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and does not find a point of pain, and it is a grievous abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance it is a grievous abscess, painful and piercing, and of bad color, and sometimes it comes from a blow on an artery, or from inflammation of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from a blow on an artery, it is recognized by the warm disposition of the abscess, when you press it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it does not seem to you that you touched it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	That which is made from inflammation of a vein is recognized by its disposition to the expression of the touch of the fingers, and one can well make an estimate about it based on this similarity, and on other symptoms.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cut the cord of the joints, then place the egg white above, and rub the dough fiercely with a white cloth, and release the suspension from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg is already mixed with these new charms, then it is necessary that you extract the egg, and cut the cord.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is stuck to the cloth, or in that which is inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you release all that tension, and cut around completely.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is where the skin is behind, then it is necessary that you cut it all, and withdraw the vein, as we have said.

de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	These are abscesses wrapped in a wrapping resembling a finger stall, with the softening of the joints, and the patient's grievance increases greatly when it worsens.

Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a high seat, then put the suspensory of the joints below your fingers, to all the vessels that are near the edge, and touch the masters, and stretch them out forcefully;

puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then heal the wound as with others or by putting a bandage, so that no vessel is injured that does not nourish one of the joints;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	because through this there comes no harm, and if all the veins are seen, then it is necessary to treat all the joints;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the eyes do not lose their nourishment through the incision of the veins, and they dry out and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the treatment of this face
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The happenings of this vein are through the section that comes out or goes back in, or the extension into the belly in the part of the gutters, because the intestines descend from that route to one of the joints;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this routing is either downwards or back in, or from the extension of it, and these two manners come from many causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	or from percussion, or from a fall, or from a blow, or from the lifting of a heavy weight, and from similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is from the extension downwards, are that it happens little by little, in long tension, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and it is equal abscesses just as far as the peritoneum, because the systolic pressure presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is a section of the syrup, which causes sudden onset of pain, and there are diverse abscesses appearing beneath the skin, close by, and this is due to the issue from the intestine and the body being weakened by the syrup.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez. Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments to fear, because they think they will escape it.

puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then put inside the leaves of the waist uncinated according to what you have need to open the wound, and be such that the eyes can issue forth;

et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and seek with your fingers if there is a point of the intestine wrapped or hard white cloth, and if you do not find anything, then thrust it into the belly below;

de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case I never saw anyone who dared to make the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old ones said that it is done as the branch which is near the vein, in such a way that you tie the veins, after cutting lightly underneath.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	then cut into the middle, and treat the abscess with what opens, until the veins are cleared.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin, as we have said, and opens the abscesses.
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and do not descend into the intestines to the intestines, and if it descends, it is little, and repair all hours.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and always if it remains too long at this point, so the wound or ulcer suppurates, as much as the intestine descends;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this happens through the extension of the ulcer that is at the angles, as we have said, because it is stretched out, then becomes softened and inflames the eyes and opens;
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	and the treatment is by cauterization, as we have said before;
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and it is never cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	and it is that the patient places his back between your hands, then takes the limb of the affected part inflamed from the large wound according to the quantity of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the ulcer that is beneath the skin where it attaches, then take the branch and put it on the limb appearing from the ulcer;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press at the deepest part of the belly, then cut the two limbs appearing from the ulcer on the head of the branch, and cut one and the other;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then extract the head of the vein, and do not cover the point from which it emerges, nor does it stretch to another thing, just as I have made you understand in the treatment of the inflammation of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Then heal by healing the wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, if it is undamaged and cures the wound, so that it becomes healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The blood flow is constricted, and has no appearance in the wound, and the cauterizations are moved to this place, and closer to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the thighs
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times are softened the skins of the hips in some men, because the flesh that is within them is softened, and it is easy to see;
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	and it is necessary, when one wants to cure, that one makes the patient sit on his back, and covers the skin that is softened with natural skin;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	then bring the two lips together at a seam, and if you see, first remove the excess of the softened skin at three seams or four firmly;
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	then cover between the seams, and heal it like the other wounds, until it is healthy, and sew the seam.
dou chastrement	two cauteries
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Be aware that I am forbidden from speaking about it in our law, and therefore it pleases me not to speak of it in this book;
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and it is not necessary to make a fuss about it for two reasons:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one of which is that the doctors know how to respond when asked and know the treatment;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often have experience of chastising certain beasts to help us, such as goat and sheep and cattle and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say therefore that chastisement is made according to two methods:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	either by attraction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the one that we make by attraction, we make the beast sit in warm water, until the joint is softened and flexible;
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then take them with your hand, until they are reset and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the correction of wounds:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	it is necessary that you hold the best, and press the skin of the joints with your left hand, then tie it with a suspensor, and cover each opening with a cup, when you have well scarified them;
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and let no pouch dwell under the syfac and the subtle syfac which is above the vessels;
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this manner of correction is better than that which is done by attraction, because in attraction something of the joints often remains, which is why the best desires luxury;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then heal the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	of hernias
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermaphroditism is in two ways among men:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	one is when between the two joints opens as if the figure of a woman's nature appears, or has hair, and sometimes the urine flows out.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has on the little finger as if a penis and two thighs.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the treatment of the shoulder and of the groin is that you should cauterize all the adjacent areas, and treat them as other wounds;
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	in the second way, for men whose urine jumps through the skin of their thighs, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tendonitis
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	A tentigen is an adjacent area on the genital part, so much that it is too ugly to see;
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and some women have it as big as a hand, and that's the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is necessary that you touch the superficies of the tentigen with your hand or with onguents, and cauterize lightly;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not go too deeply into the flesh, lest corrupted blood flows out, then treat with another treatment as long as it is healthy;
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and at another sore that is born at the mouth of the marrow, and the abscess, and by chance it bursts forth, and it is according to the resemblance of a cowe, and for this reason the ancient ones called it "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Here is the translation:
de erratique	of scarifying
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	Here is the translation:
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	and it is natural from birth, or happens by accident due to illness that comes about.
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	or it is through a displaced cartilage, or a subtle or thick douleur, and is made deep in the marrow, or in the ribs, or beneath, or as it may be.
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	and hinder conception, and impede growth, and by chance cause flowers to have.
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	and the knowledge of this is through the examination of the ulcer.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the symptoms are nearly apparent, then examine with your fingers or on the radius.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is a subtle douleur, and it is near the liver, if you hurry, and turn it thus.
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	put your two index fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs.
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	then stretch out the two livers firmly, so that the subtle douleur is round, and is above the swelling.
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	Then take the lancet, and the millstone in oil, and place it on the limb, and guide the woman to her husband each day, so that she cannot become pregnant.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the swelling is hard and thick, then it is necessary that you apply cups to the spatium-like leaves of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the swelling is from new flesh, then they suspend it from the ninth rib and the coping;
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and there are stain-releasing medicines, blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, and a mixture of many waters;
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	then insert a large poultice of plum, so that the wound cannot become septic.
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and let it be for a long time, and then insert a tent of dry flax;
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then be cured by other treatments until you are healthy.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a wound comes to the marrow, if it needs to be covered according to this method, then it is not incising enchasing abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the encasing abscess which is in the marrow, one should not touch with iron.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Hemorrhoids are overgrowths of veins without a natural adjustment, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thrombosed.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	and we have already said in the division the similarities of these, and the signs, and I will say here those which receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that embroilments and hardenings, when they are deeply rooted in the marrow, and they do not appear to sensation, if it is not a cure by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the marrow, which one can feel, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	It is necessary then that you put the woman in a cold house, next stop the flow as with tourniquets, and apply the cupping on its roots, then sprinkle medicines stopping blood flow, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things;
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	then dip her feet in cold water for an hour, then put her in cold air;
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	and if blood comes out, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and gale and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and oil, and make an plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it sticks, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If that does not work, have her apply cupping glasses to her back and do not rub her breasts with iron;
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	Then take a candle, and apply a poultice made from plantain juice or angelica juice with old wine, and set it on the wound.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess breaks, heal the wounded area thoroughly so that it becomes healthy;
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	and the one called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough, harsh head, so it must be covered as I have said previously;
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then heal it thoroughly until it becomes healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the marrow
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses occur in the marrow, such as cancer and piercing abscesses and herpes and swellings and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	It is necessary therefore that I describe in this treatise the hot abscess that comes from the marrow, which is not among the abscesses that collect pus.
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	and if you want to know the work of iron, look to see if the abscesses are agitated at the beginning of their coming, and full of bitterness and fever, and if it becomes red you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Then do not hasten to pierce, but make meure so long as the pain is assuaged.
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then make the patient sit on a chair, and have small chairs or he leans, and supports himself on his back and brings his feet together in parts of the leg;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let his thighs be expanded, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a soft linen bond;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then suck the swelling towards the right side, and I will minister the instrument through which one opens the mouth of the marrow, from which afterwards comes the form;
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you have seen to minister this instrument, you fix the rule first in order to know the depth of the marrow, so that what enters in from the instrument does not go more deeply than it should, and it does not harm the patient;
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the swellings are larger, it is necessary to cover the deepness of the thigh with bandages, so that the swellings do not cause grief.
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary to place the point of the instrument above, and to hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscesses open, and one feels it with the soft hand, then it is necessary to cover at the head, with a spatula-like sheet.
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	and when the wound is empty, it is necessary that you put in the wound tents moistened with rose oil, or with green dry oil.
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and put the tent far from the wound at the depth of the thigh, and put beneath on the thigh and on the whole clean nettle moistened in water or mallow being cooked.
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal after 2 days of anointing coming to that, until it be sound.
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and sometimes lift up the marrow and the wound with a cluster of water and honey, and then with water or roots of lilies and a long aristology so they may be cured.
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then return to the joint.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is repopened in the marrow, it is necessary to guard against cauterizing with iron, but rather cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of the swelling
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	It is better first to know the natural shape of the child's birth, and the signs are when you see the woman approach from below, and want to odor the arm.
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	then one hastens the children to issue forth strongly;
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	then one knows that this child's birth is according to the natural shape, and the issue is under its head, and the second with him;
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press his belly lightly, so that the child issues forth quickly;
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	for when he descends on his head, the second is with him, and the marrow of his superfluities is purified by good mundification;
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	For it comes sometimes upon its feet, and comes against the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes upon its belly, or waist, and is converted by chance upon its neck, and by other bad shapes;
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	it is necessary at the handling that it be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must aid them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the infant comes onto its head by natural issue, and the woman gives birth with difficulty, and the virtues of it are weak, then make it sit on a saddle, or the women hold it;
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	and raise its natural oil or fenugreek being cooked, and then put the handling between its two small spatula-like tools of which this is the form;
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and burn the second layer, and cut to his finger as much as the moisture which is inside corresponds to his fingers.
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	and pierce the belly of the woman as much as the infants are inside, and if they do not descend, then it is necessary to cleanse the woman with a mustard-based enema with oil of sesame.
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	then make her take a purge and evacuator of conditis, and hold her mouth and nostrils for an hour:
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	if the infants are now stuck.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if the two hands are frozen, it is necessary that you reset them lightly, little by little.
et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut;	and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a chair, and raise her feet high up;
puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement;	then remove the chair from the ground, and hold onto the woman, so she doesn't fall at the removal.
et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and if he cannot put his hands in, and the infant dies, if he places his hands on the counter which is placed before him, and extracts the child, and resets equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the infant comes onto its feet, then it must be pushed upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it little by little, until it is straight;
puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take its feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	When it jumps just to the hips, if he instructs to take hold, and makes it stretch out with condition;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it jumps far, so God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump frequently as we have said, then it turns a little and a little, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lighter.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier;	And if it does not come far as we have said, then take a poultice of high altitude, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and crush all in the mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	and put on the nature of the woman within and remove this ointment, then make her sit in warm water until below the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when it is softened below, have them make a collar of myrrh, and put it below, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then have them sit on a seat, then have them stretch out and hold their mouth and nose, and gently press their belly, for the infant now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child on his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the infant comes in this form, if you place the bath of his hands little by little;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit;	then be swooned on his neck, and let his feet hang down, and be reclining on the bed;
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and fold his hands little by little, and then press his hands on the belly, and lift the cushions from below, until it is prepared downwards;
