et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the infant does not jump, take his feet and move them forcefully, then move the belly upwards, then you will thrust your hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc;	and heat it little by little;
et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and instruct the woman to grasp them as much as the infants issue.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the delivery of the child who is coming out with one hand while
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is necessary to re-engage to bring back the hand:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman get up and go;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	if she cannot walk, then make her sit on a bed, and bend her legs forcibly;
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then massage the muscle that I have touched;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if she does not conceive, then make her sit on a chair, then study how to bring back the hand;
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and heat the infant according to the natural figure, and make her stretch out, and instruct her to grasp them as much as the infants issue forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the issue of the child on its neck, and it has spread out its hands, and its face turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	it is necessary that the patient holds his hand, then turn it little by little, and heat it lightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	and when it is even, then place on the natural muscle of the thigh and oil, as we have said, then instruct it to move little by little;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne;	and when you have done this, then make it sit on the seat, and instruct it to take hold;
et la fai esternuer.	and make it stretch out.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for all the secondary ones
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to be in this manner throughout the second stage, then touch the second stage with your finger, until the moisture is evacuated;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if it forms a crust on its face and neck, then touch the swelling, so that it is not retained, and soothe the inflammation;
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then put the child inside, until you have placed it as it should be, and instruct the woman to take hold never again;
adonques si istra legierement.	then it will be easier afterwards.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII;	Know that wounds often grow worse, and sometimes do not heal at all, or only partially.
et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	and this is not a strange thing, and it happens little.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are strange things, and do not live well, if they have a little name;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they should be multiplied, and are divided by the Syphac who separates them, which is tied to the belly;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they issue naturally like all things under us, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they issue grievously, thus the cure is as we have said, and let the subtle balm be, and make it smooth and light in what it does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do it thus as it brings health to salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	Sometimes they are formed in the marrow I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious sage, and it is necessary that the balm knows all this, because by chance similar things happen;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	do thus according to what is suitable.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat the woman with a dead or stillborn child in her womb, as I have said in the section, and it does not come forth, and you are forced to operate with your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is suitable that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has not had an accident or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	it is suitable that the woman be placed on her back, and her legs be bent downwards, and her thighs lifted;
et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the midwife holds the two parts, or she is tied to the bed so that she is not torn apart by the descent of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then anoint the mouth of the womb with moist oils of sage and fenugreek and flaxseed, then rub the belly with these oils and these unguents;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	Then he puts the bout in the marrows lightly, then wants him to hold his legs where the onions are, and takes care that the veins are apparent as they descend onto his head;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	if he fixes the onions in his eyes or in his neck or in his mouth or in his palate or under the beard or in the forearm or near the ribs, and if the descents are on his feet, he fixes or pricks them and thus affects the moist places;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary to hold the onion in his right hand, and put the curve between the fingers of his left hand, and he puts his whole hand lightly, and fixes the onion in none of these places that we have said, until he comes to the empty thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and it is the shape of the onion:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then fix one against another onion, or let the third be in a similar way, so that the extractions are equal;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then they steady themselves equally in moving one way and another, to issue forth, and let the uncle's teeth hold for issuing forth, as it is the form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if it stays in one part, oil the bail with some of its fingers of oil, and rub into that part, and treat the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if it does not stay in point, put this uncle or higher up, and do that until it issues forth completely fluent.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by straightening, then you must wrap around the drapil, until it issues forth completely.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	then put a bandage on the joint of the sole or at the heel, and thus you must do with the other hand, and on the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the head of the infant is large and it is constricted in the issue, or it has an assembled sharp head, then you must put the spinal spatula between your two, and make the head and extract the sharpness.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	where you take hold of the instrument that is called "almidach", because its shape comes with the instruments or surgical tools that are behind this one;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus in the same way, it makes them have a great natural head;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	and then treat the bones as tendons, and if the head slips out and it holds onto the forceps, so be careful, as much as the moisture that is or issues forth;
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	and if it cannot issue, then cut it into pieces in the muscles where you can;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	and if it is swollen in the belly or beneath the ribs, then it is necessary that you pierce it as much as the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the infant is on its feet, it is light attraction, and the adjustments at the mouth of the mother are lighter.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is constricted in the belly or in the chest, then it is necessary that you stretch it to the wrapping envelope under the hand;
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and make an incision in the belly or in the chest, as much as the moisture that flows from it;
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	and if the other limbs are numbed, and the head remains, if he puts his hand in front of the marrow, and draws it just up to the mouth of the marrow;
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	then he puts II on the jugular or XII, and draws it forth;
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	and if the mouth of the marrow is narrowed by a hot abscess that has come there, then it does not need to be operated on, but rather to be soothed with moist and fatty things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and the soothing plaisters, and apply them in gentle, softening, and moisturizing ways.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the infant is on its side, and you can put it straight, then soothe what we have said in the living infant;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	and do not have power, if you draw it forth by parts, and leave nothing of the secondary.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, steady the hands on what we have said concerning abscesses that come in the marrow;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if a flow of blood comes, it should be placed in a tight restraining bandage, and steady other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had been dead with a stillborn child, then she conceived another on top of that one, and rejected the other dead one.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, a abscess came to him in the belly, and it inflamed so much that it opened, and began to discharge greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought for a long time, and could not soothe the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and extracted a bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled greatly, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point;	I touched the wound, and I drew back my hands, until the woman was at her best point;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman remained lying thus for a long time, and then she rose up a little from the bed;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I did not recover from this chapter further than because of that which, when the masters find a strange thing, they know how to put it in aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the thigh back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres;	Hereafter comes the form of the pressor, to which one owes the books;
et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	and it is given to two turners as are the heads of the veins.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns should be more subtle on the constrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the tube be two fingers wide, and the margin of the trees it should be, and a palm and a half in length;
et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and inside the two limbs should be two adjustments of this same tube, which are closed at one end and the other, half a palm in length or a little more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	and these two adjustments are pushed into the mouth of the mortar to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, in its likeness more subtle and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of the tenacules.
et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large;	and it has two heads and two adjustments, as you see, a palm in length, and two fingers wide.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	and when you want to open the mortar with all the instrument, make the woman sit on the bed, her feet pendant and her legs covered, then push the two adjustments together into the mortar, and hold the head of the instrument down between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Then open your hand to the entire instrument, just as you have done with the equal-sized tenails, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the marrow, until the bale makes it do what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances;	These instruments are all mounted above, and are multiplied in their similarities;
et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	and when the miry ones have been prepared, so much the more hasty is the work, and the higher it stands among men according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument that you have not prepared, for its necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the second one is retained in infancy, it is necessary that you command the patient to retain his wing, and then make him stretch out his condition, and hold your hands at the mouth and nostrils;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and let it jump through that, well it is.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If it does not, take the pot, and make a perforation or covering, and put there herbs that can open the mouth of the marrow, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, sassafras, and centaury;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu;	All these herbs, or some of them, should be cut or placed under the fire;
puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris;	then put a cane or perforated tube, and the other end in the mouth of the marsh, and hold it until the vapors come out from the marsh;
puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	then make it distill, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second [injury] happens quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not get better, instruct the patient to anoint their left hand with oil of sesame or mastication of alta, and then put it in a natural place, and seek the second [remedy];
et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and when they have found it, take it and stretch it little by little, straightening it so that the marsh does not hinder the extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie;	but you must move it gently to the right and to the left, and then draw it out;
si venra et se desaerdra.	If it comes apart and falls out of joint.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the thigh is constricted there, we have spoken of the treatment of stretching, and of fumigation with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it does not respond to all that we have said, beware that you do not fall into the trap;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the thigh, you apply it to the hip of the woman, then anoint it with ointment of four herbs;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if it will putrefy and become swollen, and will come to a crisis;
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but in any case, when it putrefies thus, bad odour comes to the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	It is necessary then to use fumigations of covenaubles for this:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	none of the ancients have experienced fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument is where one fumes the woman at the retention of the flowers and of the second thing, which is this.
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is to make similar to a dog, and place the subtle head in the nature, and the large heads above the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigations be on the coals, and the blistering as long as it is roasted, and start another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation perceived, thus it has been stopped by subtle signs:
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	then it is necessary to give to the patient who perceives it thus at his finger, and does not feel it from a subtle touch, and warns of the bandage that it does not touch it;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on the affected limb in wine and oil, then the treatment of anointing until it is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not stiffen, then put or insert a poultice of warm plaster, and leave it on for many days, and be careful when the children want to go to their chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And sometimes these stoppings come suddenly from a wound or an abscess;
si covient coper celui soudement:	then it is necessary to cover that suddenly:
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	be cured, as we have said about the treatment of the spear wound.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula at the bottom foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that come from beneath the foundation are a swelling, and those that come from beneath the deep foundation are a furuncle, or in the space of the two parts, if there is one fistula or more.
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when that swelling is old, it opens, and sometimes moisture introduces a white or subtle pus, and often these fistulas are persistent.
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and they are known by the fact that there is an emission or flatulence when the patient makes an effort to vomit, and sometimes by chance it jumps up suddenly.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if there are fistulas that penetrate just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and they reach just to the joint of the thigh, and just to the top of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one recognizes the persistent fistula at the bottom, and does not miss it:
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you apply your index finger to the bottom, and insert a subtle needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is twisting, you insert a subtle probe of lead, or a horse hair, until you feel the probe or hair on your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come from bad pertussis or ventilation or vermin, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	know that it does not pierce badly;
si te haste dou curer.	if you hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is piercing near the bladder or near the urinary duct, if the urine jumps out, and it cannot be soothed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is pierced just up to the joint of the thigh, then the probe comes just to the place;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the discovery of the pain within, then it is that he immediately bows, and no medicine or sudden remedy by anointing;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these fistulas one has no cure unless they work hard, and vanity of foolish doctors who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In one that is not a persistent case and not an old one, there is hope of health through iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient places himself between your hands on his back;
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and he lifts his legs up to his knees, and has his knees inclined towards his belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then apply a straightening iron, or of lead if there is twisting, until you know where the straightening comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels it in his foundation, then you should apply your right index finger, and thus you will feel that the straightening has penetrated;
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and be discovered where you feel between your fingers the vital spirit or the flesh, then you know that it is persistent;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if one does not work on it, it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One can almost always heal everyone, but this happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help that one does, if it is that one heats the subtle cautery according to the size of the fistula, as it was said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and heat the entire area thoroughly in the fistula, until it reaches deep into the foundation;
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this two or three times, until you know that these withered fingers are scorched, which resemble a bird's claw;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat the moist gangrenous area with powder, until those fingers are dry, then treat the ointment by sprinkling and applying it suddenly.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If this, nothing else can be healed;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and hold it between, and do not pierce just to the knuckle which is at the foundation, and between your finger and the tent [probe] a thick covering of flesh or skin, and you see the fistula at that which follows the covering of the vein;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	If you cut open the beginning of the fistula, and cut ahead before the tent, and then apply the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the head of the tent.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and the tent will be freed, and will fall.
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	then I will describe those swollen veins that resemble a bird's claw, and none of them remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound does not heal, and it is short between you and the joint, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the fire cauteries assemble two bone things:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	it is to know, the art of joining these veins, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the treatment of swollen tents in mud or in broken pieces of wood, until the juices flow out, and it makes the veins dry in the mud;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound of the fingers suddenly inflamed with hard charcoal, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healthy and does not relapse again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes near the fontanelle of the fundament, and is separated from the body, then apply your finger or fundament, and inquire into that.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the tension, and between there is the cloth or the silk or flesh, or it is near to piercing, if there are no other ways of fixing and hoping, by the administration of one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize as we have said, or you cut just to the foundation, or if you can place tents and cure as before;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too deep in the foundation, lest you cut the holding that holds the base, and come upon the evacuations by the senses willingly;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then the cure, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	by chance it will be healthy, or you remove that covering and the world then it is cut from the deep foundation, either by tent or by another sharp instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then I will define the faulty flesh which is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	Then study to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the part that is below the foundation.
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is something lighter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And often they are fistulas according to this method:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it is or costs against the foundation below, so take a perforated tent at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And thrust the twisted thread into the fistula, and thrust the tent into the entire thread in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation within, then extract the thread of that perforation, so that you push your finger or foundation;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and pull the head of the thread, and assemble the two joints together, and hold one to the other, and leave it a day or two;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it often, until the threads absorb the flesh that is between them, and heal.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	Then heal the wound until it is sewn up and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not penetrate, then make it penetrate in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not suit to make a copper plate for the ulcer's dressing too deep inside, and then heal it, as we have said, so that it becomes healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spatula-like instrument that one uses to make a fistula is very sharp at one end and cutting;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and not on the other side, because one should not cut where one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of the wounds
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Embrodings are in two manners:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	where they are deep in the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they cut short the blood flow, and there is one or more, and they are deficient in the foundation and at the head of the foundation;
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are deficient have little moisture, and they cut short either a little of citrine water or a little of blood, and they have the color of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment of those who have them deep in the foundation, is that you instruct the patient to stretch out in a chamber, until the foundations issue forth, and they appear as threads;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you hurry, and bend it as tendons, or you hold it with your fingernail, then he covers it in its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the tendons cannot hold them back by their moisture, if they take it to the apron, or to the cushion, or to a piece of chamelot;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and stretch it with your fingers, then cover, and sprinkle above some hot powders that are in the fire of cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize it as it is said or chapter of cautery, then heal other wounds until he is healthy;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot issue, then cleanse the patient's fundament with a biting and harsh clyster, to wash what is in the foundation, so that it can open freely;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient cannot pass, and if the veins are far from the fundament, then it is a light cure;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them with your fingernail or with the tenaculum, and you cut, then you cure as we have said, until they are healthy, and they fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	It is necessary that you adjust the splint according to this method:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take a twisted thread, and put it on a needle, and then pull the thread above and make a piercer pass through the needle from another side, and twist the two ends of the thread below the needle, and so it is doubled in size;
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and hold the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and withdraw the needle, and do thus for all the others, and leave one to correct the excessive flow of blood;
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation a soft cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient that they should rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it rest as long as it heals, and when they are calm, if the treatment of bandaging and other treatments, as long as it becomes healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	you must drain thoroughly at the bottom or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is draining of flux in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you reach the tip of a spatula or your finger under the scab, which does not allow it to become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat it as long as it becomes swollen, as it is necessary.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot swell, recommence the rubbing more strongly than before, as long as it discharges much and becomes scarred.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it as long as it becomes healthy.
dou fremit	due to trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formication is a small faulty appearance beneath the skin, and it goes very deeply inwards;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it finds the cold place, and one feels it as if dead from cold, and it comes into all of the body, and more in the hands than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a vein from a goose's wing or a strong vein from a vulture, and place that vein on the frigid area, so that the purple circles encompass the entire frigid area;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand all around the vein so that you grasp everything entirely around the frigid area, and place it in the foreground, and scrape the frigid area of its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make a cane of iron or copper according to this form, and be subtle underneath and draw above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	do not pierce, because you must hold at the finger, and press strongly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see, if you cauterize the frigid area, as it is before or in the chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cluster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Never make a cluster of silver or copper, or of melted tin or lead;
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and never make any of these small and large instruments, according to those for which they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These are the things one uses to treat children who are weak and painful, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the enema device is small and large above, where the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and there is a disunion where the intestines are tied, as you see, and the chest is perceived from within;
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and it has one of the ribs pierced, and in the other I;
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and it has the intestines where one puts medicines in a bladder of beast or parchment, and it is perceived all around with small piercings, and there is between each piercing I ought to space, then insert into these piercings I strong thread twisted from X or within, and assemble the intestines as if it were a tube;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is inside, then tie it to the instrument in front of with a strong thread, then inject;
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and that's the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be not too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or albumen of egg, or similar thing, then insert it gently;
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	Then the practitioner prepares his hands together, so that they are completely steady, then extracts the lancet, and lifts the patient's legs to the bench, and if the medicine wants to exit, it will do so as much as it can.
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps a night completely, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cleanse him of the disease of bowel disorder, and the medicine hastens to be issued, so recommend it as much as he may be healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are at the foundation, or an abscess, so let the lancet be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and it is the shape of the subtle lancet on which the skin should be held firm.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have already spoken about the treatment of wounds in the previous section.
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	Now we will tell you about the treatments of hands and of medicine, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the locations or where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by blow of stone, and cut of sword and of dagger, or of lance or of stick or of arrow, or of similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	where they are made according to the laws of the body, as it is a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the feet, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come back to its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if you take care it's not a fracture of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely broken and the wound is large, and you doubt strongly about an abscess being hot:
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if it makes the cephalic mixture healthier meanwhile if there comes little blood from the wound, and let the healing be contrary to the injured part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and avoid giving the patient a full meal of wine and coarse meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to get better, let his food be diminished, and do not drink any wine, nor eat any meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound, apply a warm compress, or cotton soaked in rose oil or violet oil, or wine steeped in it;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no warm abscess, put on the wound, so it is fresh in all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will tell a little about later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the wound is moved, put on some ointments, until it be healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword cut and similar, and the edges cannot be assembled by tugging, then assemble them by suture, as I will say for wounds of the belly, from the suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is uncovered from the bone, and it bursts, and no longer holds except for a little, then cover it.
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, as if testing and roasting cooked, just like poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a skin lesion, and it does not adhere to the bone, so scrape off the entire lesion, and apply a poultice, then treat.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if it has become embedded in the wound or vein, without being able to cut it out, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, so try to remove it, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if that does not benefit, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and it is that you apply this powder which sticks thus that the wound will close.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the manner of the powder is:
pren encens une partie;	take incense, a part;
sanc de dragon II parties;	Dragon's blood, two parts;
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	living chalk, three parts, and powder subtly, and fill the wound, and hold it firmly, until it heals well and joins all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then lay it well, and let it not swell;
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	for one does not stop the medicine until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never does one make a poultice of chalk solely, when one has not incense nor dragon's blood, but rather the arsenic has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the arsenic has touched the wound, especially in this case, then do not put any of this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digested ointments, or powders made from water and honey of barley, until it brings forth a scab;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal with other treatments until it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about the fractures of the head afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, then there is no other remedy than to leave the treatment, and not to put anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of it is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be soothing, as if warm water is poured gently, and mixed with rose oil, and cooled in gentle water, and other minerals of mine according to this manner, and moist unguents.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it up with bandages, then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is hairy and full of pus, then pierce or cut below the hair;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and blood flows out, then stop it, and bind it, and cauterize, for that is the trade;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the jugular vein, and the conduits are guarded, because that's where the flesh goes, then sew up the jugular vein on the canal of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then he holds it firmly, and leaves it for some days, then cures the wounded place so that it be healthy;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, seek it;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are pieces of bone, remove them gently so you can, and those that you cannot have, leave until the wound putrefies, and separate and alleviate the discharge;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder that I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has become fistulous, then treat it as I have said in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a wound from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, look to see if the wound has any windiness where the patient's breath passes through:
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	know then that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put the powder on it at the first hour, nor bind it with a bandage that does not absorb the blood that flows deeply, and revives the heart, and kills the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but I put an attractive ointment, and apply it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you have no ointment, put a lot of cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if no spasm comes, nor bad trembling of the heart, it is not a sign of evil origin;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good signs, know that the wound is healing.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal the thumb of tendons and other cures, until it be sound;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, and ulcerate, then know that there is a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	if the cure is as one ought.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, or in the chest or back, then cure those that are in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	If it is large, of a suture;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, of powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and in having taken pieces, so that the wound closes, and the torn fibers are reunited;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not reunited, let the wound putrefy, thus alleviating the extractions;
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and of other wounds to other limbs is the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	because of the obstruction of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are large and medium and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the large wound sometimes the intestine, or the nerves of the intestines, because of the introjection of them;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the sewing is more troublesome, and sometimes it is better to have a small wound than a large one, because one puts the intestines back in place more easily, if one does not put them back hurriedly;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	Here is the translation:
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And you know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	the two common stitches have in the stitching of the belly, and the stitching of other wounds of the body and the two other proper stitches are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and however they are more proper with the stitching of the belly, and I will describe each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine is outside, and easy thing is to repair, it is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in such a manner:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	soak a sponge or a piece of cloth in hot water only slightly, or you cook in hot water squinancy and cypress and spike, and lift up the intestine until the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and often makes these veins retract, and it is murdered that they are loosened by desinflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the inflammation departing, if you moisten the intestine with water or wine and bad humors are cooked, because by this the entry is aligned to a small thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a little wound at the instrument by which one gathers the hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is murdered that the cutting, that we must not cut without great necessity there is;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and these are the instruments for making a fissure:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut within the curve and do not stray, and see there the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine bursts forth, if you reset it according to its natural form in its proper place, you should be able to put it back, for that is worth much.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, then you must make the patient sit on his back, and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the lower part of the belly, set the head and the foot higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts then put attention to this, so that the injured part may be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say in large wounds and injuries.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	For small wounds, use what appears suitable to you, then hold it between your hands and apply gentle pressure that touches the entire rupture with your hand, and bring the lips together;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common method of sutures, and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave at the head of the wound a space of two fingers, and insert a needle or have a strong thread.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the siphac, which is beneath the skin within, until you make it pierce through that part, and join the two heads of the siphac together with the four.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then strain with a double thread beneath the needle of two parts, then assemble the two heads of the wound gradually, and then leave the finger of space, and fix another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then thread the second string just as you did with the first needle, and do not cease from doing so according to what you have mastered of needles, until the entire wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be moderate, between subtle and coarse, for the subtle needles grasp all the flesh, and those that are too coarse cannot enter well;
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Because it is necessary that they be moderate;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not necessary to push the needles too deeply into the flesh and soft skin, lest they grasp and open the wound before the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then grasp the heads of the needles, so they do not bother the patient while sleeping, and put tents or drapes on the heads of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is sewn;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of treating with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it suffices to use a single needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second treatment is common, and it is where you bring together the two heads of skin and the two heads of the superficial fascia, assembling them to one needle or having a strong middle thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have pierced these heads all four together, then reassemble the needle at the part where you began, in the manner of sewing clothes.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space between each stitch the width of a smaller finger.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	this stitching suits the man, and I sewed a wound that a certain man had in his belly, which was injured by a knife, and it was more than a palm in length, and it was two palms deep into the intestines, and it was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I will bring back the intestine then when it had been stopped for 24 hours, and the wound was sewn up to 15 days, and it healed, and was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they looked at him who was judged to die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not care for his treatment, because I stood in the place where they did not find any, nor any medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and applied sense upon the wound cotton very little twice a day, and washed with warm honey water until he was healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and sew up the defective part just to that inner depth;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the right heart in a straight line, if you have sewn up the head of the siphac or stitched or you have sewn with the needle, and make it pierce another part of the defective inner area;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the intention of this suturing is that you sew thus as the pelletier makes the pellets, and that you leave one time the siphac of one part, and take it again from another, until the suturing is entirely complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second way of suturing, which Galen described properly, is like no other font, which naturally assemble the two parts together, and apply one head to the other head, in such a manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Take a needle or a head of a mirror close by, and make it pierce the limb only slightly, and let the two heads of the suture;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the weak part just up to there within, as the two heads of the suture;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make one and the other pierce from the weak part just up to there within, in the two other heads of the mirror that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and it is the worst way of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	Galen said this in his speech, and none of them testify, that one should sew the belly with two needles, or thread in each.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must thrust a needle from one side, and another from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the rupture is within the belly, it is the suture more grievous than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, just as the arrow had moved, then reset the intestine, and the skin;
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then put on the powder soothing charm, and if the arrow had moved, then put on no ointment that is present, until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the thread, and be sewn the seam, and the membrane;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the wound as with the others, until it is healthy;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you have no medicines, put them on, as soon as it begins to gather pus, much cotton, and change it twice a day so that it be healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no other remedy in many cases when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound will not make a community with the principal members, then it is necessary that you anoint lightly with oil of tempered heat, or oil of rose, and put it between the limbs, and beneath the wounds;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if it feels pain or bloating in the belly, and many times it happens, then they are cleansed with red wine enema, and meanwhile the bloating reaches just up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and it pierces within, and knows that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeune" cannot heal when it is wounded, and it is because of the abundance of veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the approaching of its nature to the kidneys.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if he jumps away from the wound, set him back just like the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and has turned towards black, then you must lay the black spot, from which the blood flows, for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut what is between the ligament, and place the two heads hanging down from the part below the wound just until it reaches to ease the extraction when the hairs fall, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture from the swelling
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some homes, because I saw that a man was wounded or pierced by a lance in his belly;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it was the wound on the right of the stomach, and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and thus stopped the evacuation and the flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I make a cure according to what I can do, and did not cease from subtling until it was healthy, and the eyes were sound.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it sounding, I doubted that the patient had a bad condition in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but he remained in better disposition, and was eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and certain experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied up in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take firm threads, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the thread has covered the mouth, place it on the two lips, so that it draws its mouth together;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cover the head, and it holds so that it cannot dislodge, then put another thread afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is entirely closed;
et cout la plaie.	and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the intestine is torn inside, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a subtle thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a manner:
