pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Take the head of this intestine thread that is very clean, and then tie it to the head of this twisted subtle thread, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and reset it in its place;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of suturing the intestines is not forced except according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the gut intestines, if there is no ingenious way to heal it, except with subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whether it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes inflamed, is universally called "fistula", and similarly when it is hairy and produces a swelling.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is according to the true notion of a hard and white scab, where one does not feel pain, and it is also shaped like the feather of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in a clear hollow, and another time thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and another time enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have already spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healthy, and there is no flesh, this is only due to one of the 8 causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	it is to know, by the small passage of blood or flow;
ou por sa malice;	or through its badness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much hollow;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the liquid is putrid, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a kind of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is slow in digestion, and slow in health, and weak by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the treatments of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is fitting that I teach you about the treatment of fistula which is done by surgical operation with hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all tender parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that come from the large veins, and from the arteries, and from the nerves, or in the spleen, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it happens that it comes to the property of the principal member, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is a fistula that does not come near the place I have told, and you have confidence in the cure, and you know how to recognize it, if you take a thread of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, if you seek;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is twisted, seek a subtle tenderness of pricking, because the pricks pierce much into the twist.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if the fistula has many perforations and you cannot explore well by pricks, then cleanse it through one of the perforations, because moisture runs from one perforation to another, and it is clarified.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then ask for the power of your judgment, that you know if there is bone or nerve, and it is cut off in the deep, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is near a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the putrid flesh and the corrupt humors that are within.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the treatment so that it be healthy, and if the fistula is well perforated in the right place, then you must cut deeply, as much as you can, then you put tentacles of medicine ague, and the joints just at the head of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the superfluity which remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put ointments in a healthy clear skin, so that it be healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not healthy through this, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve grieves or principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then remove it as much as the corruption is entirely removed, then treat the things in a healthy clear skin so that it be healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not healthy, and renders void thus as before, know that you have not been misled just until now
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if it becomes uncovered and seeks as much as you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the joint
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healthy, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot come to it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can treat it with tongs, if it is suited to the instrument convenient for that, and if there are many bones, treat them all, do not leave any behind;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if the moisture makes it contrary, and there is no error or fear, if it is moist and dry and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot dislodge them at one hour, then put on the wound a poultice that promotes suppuration, and let it be until the abscess is formed around the bone, and then they will have less difficulty with the bones.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, then remove so much of the decay until the blackness is entirely removed, then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the corrupted bone, and it reaches to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is necessary to saw and cut all the way to the corruption, and then to cure until it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so much that the materials came to the leg, and it was inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no way to remove it by surgical opening.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the mirror shows them by their foolishness overpowering so much that the abscesses open, and they corrupt many materials, and become fistula, and it comes from many perforations that everything goes to waste and moisture of the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many a mirror that mirrored a cure within 12 years, and there was no wisdom in the art of hands, so much that I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was treated, and those that corrupted through the perforations to a great body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young patient would become red, and had a yellowish tint.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I thrust a probe into one of these holes, and then explored all the holes, and found that one vein came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I hastened then, and cut into one of the perforations as far as I discovered a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came just to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw that which appeared to me from the corrupted bone, and believed that there was no other corruption, except for that which I had seen;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and begin to restore the wound with medicine soaks for a long time, and cannot be sutured;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the continued corruption in the bone, and the decay, and then I stopped, and thought about suturing the limb;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not do so much that I grasped around a palm of the bone, and pulled it out with all its thickness, then restored it with medicines;
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it was healed and sutured quickly, and did not need to begin the work again for the faintness of the patient, who could not suffer, and for fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because the bloody evacuations often occur, but it was entirely healthy, and a hard crust formed on the bone, and was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction in everything, neither to alleviate nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take a lien, and hold it at the head of the bone that is open, and instruct him to stretch it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and put another thicker bandage on top of the first one, and tie it to the flesh that is above the bone, and tighten the head, so that you draw out the corrupt flesh from below, and uncover the flesh on the spot where you see swelling, lest the swelling burst the flesh;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a probe or a tube below the bone to drain out the corrupt flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and thus it is necessary to explore as one can see and feel the corruption, and explore again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then uncover the whole flesh;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then put a probe below, and then explore from one part to the other for the corruption, and be the surgeon who removes the length of the corrupted part, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut off the corrupted joint, and sew up the bone or where it connects to the other part;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, then there is no other remedy than to amputate;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand or finger of the foot, then it is very strong that thing, but anyway it is necessary that you investigate that corrosion, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and treat it in all the ways that you can, but make sure the vein or nerve does not work against you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and know that the incisions and the seams to cut these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of the holes, and their thickness and their subtlety, and their size and their smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore he must prepare each similar appearance of work his instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and know that the work will show you the instrument you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and it will testify to the methods of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you prepare the instrument you will need according to what he requires.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The heads perforate either because of denseness or because of fierceness;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have medicated that corrosion by the treatment of medicines, and it does not benefit, if it is necessary to amputate that member up to where the corrosion comes from, so that the patient escapes death or malice, which is greater, from the defect of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are that the members turn black, as if they were burned by fire, and afterwards the blackness spreads, since it goes from one member to another, and takes over the whole body;
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you hasten to cover, and it is by the percussion of certain venomous beasts, like scorpion of sea and viper and similar, if the corrosion is at the head of the finger, if you touch, do not give it space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, if you touch at the joint, so that the corrosion does not reach up to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, if you touch at the elbow;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and no remedies are of use except the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and thus always do when the corrosion reaches to the foot:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes to the first joint, then touch after another joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then touch the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and let it rise in the leg, if it gathers at the joint of the knee;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and let it come above the knee, if there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the way to bandage or to splint the limb is that you bind it above and below, and extend one minister below the lower ligament, and another minister above the upper ligament, and you separate the flesh that is between the two ligaments at a spacious interval, so that the bone may be uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then bandage or splint, and put a layer of linen on each part, so that the splint does not touch the healthy skin, and comes to the patient with another wound and abscess thus.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if a flow of blood comes when you operate, then cauterize the skin hastily, or apply some restraining powders above.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine as long as it is accomplished, then tie the numb member with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healthy.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will count that it had an ounce of powder in that pie:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	it had a blackness that seemed to be burnt by fire, and that corrosion came first in his finger near the pie, so much that it seized the whole pie;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover the pie, and was healthy;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long after that the corrosion returned to his hand, and it came to me, and I put on things receptive to the purification of the body, but could not stop the corroisons;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he saw that I was treating his hand, and I did not want that, for I had hoped to repulse the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I doubted also that he cut off his hand, so it wouldn't die, because the strength of the man was feeble;
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he despaired at once, and returned to his land, and ceased to coop up his hand, and was healthy;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not counted it a failure because of this that one does another task, if one has mastery.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	At no time did an abscess come on the flesh, and it stayed so long that it made a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it burst and pierced, and the pus jumped out, and the veins were empty, just like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin which is above is as subtle as the delicate sheets, and does not corrode to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy", and is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so enlarged that it reaches just to the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin if it is that you cut entirely around, and likewise when it is subtle, just like a thin sheet;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not be afraid of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you think that the skin is rotten, and the corruption is not in depth, and the skin is thick with flesh, then heal it with a poultice thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	look if the wounds are large, and the pus that is in them is of foul odor, then cleanse with a medicine made from Egyptian remedies, which is thus prepared:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take ashes, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put skin in a vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take of this according to your necessity, and make it into a point and in the middle, and cleanse the wound, and hold back the pus;
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine sit for two hours, then wipe it off by sprinkling;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the wound is made whole, and the pus is gone;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and no time is cleansing with water of ashes, when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes of vine wood, and pour water on them, then stir, and cleanse, until you know that the wound is well healed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes, then cleanse with water and honey, or where there is a little bit of crushed litharge;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	where you mix honey and wine in a blend, so that the honey has properties of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the healthy.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you are confident that the wound is well cleansed, if you blend what makes flesh grow in it, and it is that you take a plaster made with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	where you blend some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have described in the treatise on ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the opening of the wound is small, and the cane of the syringe cannot enter, then enlarge it a little with an iron tool, and apply there a tents of Egyptian ointment, or royal balsam ointment, until it is enlarged;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too large, then sew it up and let it heal so much that the syringe or cane can enter, and if the opening that gushes out is above, then cover or apply below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the belly is in depth, if he does not let it swell there;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cover the lower back in this way as you see, it appears in such a manner that the belly reaches the lowest place it is, for when the belly is in depth, if he does not let it swell there; and if you cannot cover the lower back in this way as you see, it appears in such a manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	that the belly reaches more lightly downwards, and does not let anything of the belly;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and stretch over it a layer of linen that covers the whole wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then cover the forces in the right place of the deep wound as much larger than at first, then stretch a soft ointment over another layer according to the quantity of the wound, and put it on the wound of the belly to alleviate it, and do not remove the large bandage except after many days once;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and he who is above the breast's pertussis, often suffers to open the bowel, and knows that which runs from the bowel, whether it be venom or little or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take heed that the patients feel pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been extended in such a manner and you see the nature that jumps upon the breast's pertussis, then knows that the breasts have altered already, and approaches health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then loosen it in the morning, or the third day, and when you open the wound, if you change to another dressing, and renew the binding.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if his senses are bewildered indignant after many days, know that his senses are not yet clear.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if you come subtly to a long tension, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are men who delay in healing their wounds, and of those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the bowel is undigested it jumps from the breast after many days, knows that the breasts have not altered;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the senses are slow to understand, and it is delayed, if you add medicines which are moist in substance and dry in virtue, as we have defined, because there is a great part of glass, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take a definite ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the juice of much wine equal in substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then congeal it and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and this same thing makes honey cakes thick, when definite ointments are not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them, and powder them over the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then glue it to the plaster, and apply it to the breast, and many times it helps an Aristologist, and celestial roots, which is also like flour of veins and a hundred;
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in use of simples or of compounds:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I have said, and in use;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the wound is lengthy, and it is not cured by this treatment, then know that the corruption has penetrated deeply, and makes an impression on the bone, or on the hard members, or on the ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess on the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarice is an abscess that grows under the nail of the thumb or toe, or happens by chance to grow in other fingers;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is enveloped, and one does not take care, if it comes to the abscess thus, and corrodes and eats away so much that it corrodes the root of the nail, and by chance it corrodes everything;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and there come the ulcers up to the bone, as long as it comes to painful swelling, and is the head of two large fingers, and is the color dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit at all, it is necessary that you cut away all the excess flesh that remains on the finger, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauteries are great aid if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail presses on the flesh inside, and it begins to prick, and the blister, then you must put the straight edge underneath the nail so that it does not touch the flesh, and bend it upwards, and carefully and gently lift the subtle flesh, and apply the remaining flesh with burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the wounded areas until they are healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, you will cover it, and pull hard, for as much as the bone is corrupted it is, so it cannot be healed;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see the finger corrupting, cover it with one of our remedies as mentioned before, then heal it until it is healthy;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if he is bruised, and swollen, and feels great pain, then it is necessary that you soothe him first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the edge of the spatula obliquely while cutting across, and beware that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the ankle, for the patient would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on it to calm it down.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain that comes from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all flesh, and by chance they have a part where they have bones, and sometimes they have an angle, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is not in any of us from the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	He who is born without a nail on the finger does not move it, and he who is born with a joint on the finger, perhaps moves it;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut of one who is fleshy is light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	if you hold it with a copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In one that is born with a toe in the back node, it is necessary that you first cut the round flesh up to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable joint for that, then cure until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sudden pains that come together arise from birth, or from sudden wound, or from burn by fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If you know how to bind this wound, then you must repair it according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two clean cloths or moistened drapes in rose oil, so they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two subtle pieces of plaster, until the wound is closed, as it is fitting.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	they suddenly come together with the palm, if they grasp that joint so it is necessary.
des vils	the bad ones
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	They are gross, swollen veins full of superfluous melancholic fluids that come into many parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they happen more in the legs of those who go on foot and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you administer sometimes purging of the intestine, and then the blood of the basilica vein.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The iron treatment is according to two manners:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is that they are bound, and one draws out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you raise the vein, and draw it out entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cutting is done according to this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Raise the leg first with a warm, very hot, towel, so that the gross sinew becomes subtle, then stretch the patient's leg from above the hip down to the part beneath the knee;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then cut the vein in I, II or III, with a large incision, then release and draw out black blood at your hand, from one head to the other, until as much of the blood as the patient's virtue can suffer;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then lay him down, and instruct him to abstain from eating black bile-inducing foods;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommence the evacuation and bloodletting when the veins are full, and annoy the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The elevations of the bone are done according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Raise the patient's leg, if it has a lot of hair, then put it in a bath, and raise the leg with a warm, hot towel, until it becomes red, and inflates the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bone, if you heat with fire, and then touch the vein at the bottom of the long thigh at the knee, or in the part below the joint;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the ankle, and scrape the vein of each part, until it appears as one feels;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it is seen red and black, and when it enters under the skin it seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then apply the treatment below, until it is raised from the skin, and then bend it at the ankle more lightly, then touch it in another place above three fingers;
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it with the razor, as you have done, and bend it to another ankle, as you had done previously;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then touch another incision, or more if you have mastery of it, then lift it, and touch the toe of the foot, then pull and lift up to the second incision;
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then strip the patient to the waist, as long as it takes full strength, then the scalpel;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot draw and lift it, if you push a needle to the strong double thread, and tie and pull, and you push underneath, and turn your hand from one side and the other, as long as it takes;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and beware that it does not cut, for if it cuts, you cannot draw or lift, and harm comes to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have entirely drawn it, then put on the place of the wound a clean linen cloth soaked in wine and rose oil;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat until it is healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and rolled up together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must bend it straight, but do not cut it;
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and the treatment thus as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron that one uses to open the vein is curved, and does not cut, so it does not cut the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of large curvature, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but being large as we have said, and this is the form.
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is in the legs, in warm regions where there are no herbs nor trees, and in earth where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and perhaps grows in another part besides the legs, and this comes from the putrefaction that arises beneath the skin, as it comes from within the serpent-like and worm-like courses, growing between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a great inflammation comes into the leg, then it changes the joints, and the vein begins to issue forth, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the head opens, it is necessary that you envelop around a piece of cloth one and a half inches long, and the knot, and leave the cloth on the leg, and all the times when there is no deficiency, if you envelop around the cloth, and the knot.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remainder, and do not cut it in its root, until it is entirely extracted.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it returns to the flesh, and causes an abscess and putridity in the limb, and a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and it happens often with this vein when it is treated with a long lancet, or with X, and a man came to me who had an issue with X fingers long, and when you cut it, the reason bursts out or perforates, and pierces all the way to the bottom, so that everything flows out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and let the material that is inside be evacuated, and mix in the limb medicines that prevent putridity any day, then heal as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And at no time does the vein often break, and likewise when it opens in the joint of the foot, or of the hand, and much pain comes from it, and therefore it jumps often;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Cure then the fingers thus as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of wounds that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "disease of the ox", because it has often affected the oxen, and it is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, and travels throughout the whole body ascending and descending, and one feels it well as it passes from member to member, until it dislodges the skin or where it goes, and jumps suddenly;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is generated by putrefaction of certain humors, just as come worms and serpents and lice and ascarids in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and doubt not of its malice, for when it travels through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it comes to the eye, by chance returning, and destroys the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and there are often times
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see that it is curing and treating, if one cannot do better than when it was:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	it is necessary then that you lift the limb above and below with a strong and tightly bound bandage, then cope with it and treat it firmly, and if the vein is deeply in the flesh, and you do not find it, if you cauterize with fire above, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does, is that it corrodes the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or approaching near the eye, hold the eyebrow firmly below him, then cope with it, and treat it firmly;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary to use the patient's purification of body by medicines that dissolve bad humors, and beware of eating foods that cause putridity.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes into some members, and then moves from member to member;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I see this which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and I examined her arm, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and I soon saw, as it were, a vein rising like a worm at the shoulder, swifter than anything, like living silver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then soon after spread throughout the whole body, until it came into the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it often turned back towards the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very amazed at how it moved in this way from member to member, for I had never seen this illness behave in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I had wanted to know well how the pain moves from one place to another, but I did not know it, as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and uncovered veins, and therefore appeared constrained by this wind;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and I did not appear to follow this reason according to those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and recovered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you want to cure this disease, and the patients feel that pain, it appears to you as we have said, if you lift up and down quickly, and then cut above so that this windy constriction releases at the site of the injury;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the site;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it with your eyes, so the treatment of that which drives out windiness, such as foul-smelling pills, and serpent's pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of their is that there are those which have large points, and small, and curly, and swollen;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those with elbow joints, and of those with knee joints, and of those where there are broken pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that which falls in no member if it falls according to two manners:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	where the principal member is injured, such as head, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls therefore in no place of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you about afterwards, appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many ways;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply in, then pull it out, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the signs of the head when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and falls upon the brain, are when there is concussion and swelling and inversion and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and perturbation of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps it happens without force of the nostrils, or of the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it affects the speech and the voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumps from the white moist spot resembling an abscess, and jumps out as if breaking through skin;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and it is a sign that appears, if you hold back from the treatment, and extract the arrow so it does not remain.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the arrow when it falls into the body are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not soft.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow moves as if it were an abscess, and cuts out black blood, and brings on chill and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	you will then feel no doubt that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the arrow that never leaves the forearm are that without flatulence of scum bursts from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes deeply and seeks the cold region.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the bladder, it is between the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and gives great numbness and great pain and sighs;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and moves all the shoulder members.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead remains in the stomach, perhaps it bursts from the wound some undigested food matter.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead is in the chest or belly, and there is no escape from the intestine's route, then there is no hope for a cure, nor in the extraction of the arrowhead.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrowhead remains in the bladder, and the urine jumps and comes back, and the patient feels strong pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, as with the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the joint and the spine of the back and the forearm and the elbow and the legs, and the similar limbs, are safe according to several dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrowhead is in a nerve or an artery, and it is not venomous, thus I will tell you what happened to me, because that's how you should do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man who had an arrowhead shot into the root of the nail:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I touched it, and drew it out from beneath the fat of the ear, and it was healed without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I drew out an arrowhead that had shot into the fat of the eye beneath the skin beneath, and the arrowhead was repulsed, and I could not touch it except for the point towards the wood, and it was a large arrowhead from a Turkish bow, with a very light iron without ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	I was healthy, and no evil accidents happened to me.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow at the ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I shaved the beards, and subtly touched until I extracted it, and the Christian was healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I extracted an arrow from the man whose head or belly it was piercing, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change at all;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut around the arrow, and I dislodged it, and I extracted it forcefully, and there was no evil accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man whose arrow falls on his back, and the wound was swollen above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained within him, and he did not change his natural disposition, nor did I find harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you see another man, who had an arrow shot into his face, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and he lingered thus, suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And he extracted an arrow from the king's prince's hand, which was stuck in his nail, and it was slightly leaning to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was entirely removed.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to the treatment after it had been stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very constricted.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I applied a subtle tension, and I did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt piercing pain and hurt beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the point of the arrow I put on the affected area a topical plaster, attractive and digestive, because the wounds did not become inflamed;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and it appears to me the abscess of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the plaster on the wound yesterday, and redressed the wound itself, and afterwards the patient felt the arrow for a long time, until he felt it in his nose.
et il le me dist.	and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put a corrosive medicine on the wound for many days, until it was opened, and I touched it, and felt the head of the arrow which had lodged in the flesh.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I probed into the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it went beyond the limits for four months, and then I enlarged the wound if I touched the tendons, and moved them from one side to the other, but could not remove it.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Then I did not cease to refine and to engineer in ways of instruments, until I took it the next day with well-made tenailles, according to what its form would come at the end of this chapter, until I treated it, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the mirror shows that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then restored it, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you put your treatment on what I do not say, for the book cannot take everything in.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the wise masters compare well a little great thing, and on what is present and failing, they find new work, and new instrument, at the understanding of the strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not issue from limbs where they are fixed except according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the soil or they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps forth where it enters, it is an arrow entering into their flesh, and it does not jump forth at any time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump now, let it be so that the flesh is purified around it, and may its exit be eased;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and thus if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot exit, let it be so for some days, and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps, and if it does not jump, pierce around it with a subtle iron, so that the flesh around it is enlarged, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes just to one of the vents of the brain, and none of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	Do not pull it back, but let it be until it is even after some days, for if the arrow-head comes just to the surface, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck deeply in the bone, and does not come up to there, and the patient remains for some days without bad accident, then prepare to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very deeply fixed and cannot issue forth, then administer tareres around, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure the wound until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow-head is embedded in the body of the corpse so that one cannot see it, then seek it everywhere with a probe.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then draw it out with a suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound, and due to the depth of the arrow-head, and there is no bone or nerve, then make an incision until the wound is large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and draw out the arrow-head if you can, and if it has in the arrow-head hooks by which it holds, then remove the flesh that is fixed to two parts of the muscle where you can, and then break or bend the hooks of the arrow-head, so that you can extract it.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and subtly understand that you do not break the arrow, that you remove it more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at one time, let it remain until the surrounding flesh is purified, then extract it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood makes you act contrary, then amend what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of the incision of the nerve and vein, and set in motion how you can safely remove the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient according to the position he was in when the arrow fell on him, for it is the greatest aid that it be so, and if you cannot, then arrange him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, where it appears to be nothing of his, or the skin is swollen in that place if one sees or feels it outwardly.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Cut then above, so that the tongs can grasp, and then it is stretched.
si saut fuer maintenant.	If it bursts forth now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand roundly so that it enters into the bone, and enlarges the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot exit, let it be left again, and then resume the extraction until it bursts forth;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is there, push it back into the whole shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the shaft is short, and you want to administer a push, if you administer the instrument skillfully, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then push forth, and if the arrow is shaved, push the instrument to the entering point, to alleviate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, it is necessary that you cut around the whole flesh where the veins are, so you can, then heal the wound as it fits.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is short or heavy or in the belly or in the bladder or in the side, and it is close by, and you can cover above, push it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of touching the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, such is the craft;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment until it be healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs with which one extracts arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and you see its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, middle-sized, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the instrument for extracting is like the claw of an eagle's foot, to grasp at the point of the arrow, as it is the shape.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for pushing and for extracting, that's how it is:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	Of the veins from which one bleeds are 31, where there are 16 main ones, it is to know:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	two veins that are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two temples apparent;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the two eyebrows of the two eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is in the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the head of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two bandages which are at the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the head, and laypeople call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the median is called "faste", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and laypeople call it "vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic is on the right side, and laypeople call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the fossa, and it is the one from which they bleed, which appears manifestly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the savior is the vein which is between the auricular and the anular, and if it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and where the feet are, there are three veins:
