l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is beneath the curve of the left thigh on the left side, and the second Sophia which is at the ankle of the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "nese", which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The health of the veins that are behind the ears helps against ancient catharrhes, and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of the health, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	Then he tightens the patient's neck to a vice, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in the two dependent dew-collecting vessels of the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	where the tubes reach your finger, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, it is a sign of an inch;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet and insert it beneath the vein just up to the bone, then lift your hand above the whole vein, and cut and open the skin and the vein well, two inches deep, and make the blood flow out until you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then stop it and hold it, until it is healthy;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said about incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The health of the two arteries that are in the temples, if it is to emigrate an old and worn-out optic nerve, and accustomed to obtalmia, and in the course of tears, it affects the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the healer is thus as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient strains his neck, so much that the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel beneath your finger, and then make a sign of engraving;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the heart up to the vein above your finger's index, and insert the lancet beneath, and lift the vein above, and the cupping, just as you have done in the other veins, and make the flow of blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then lower the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then place on cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then form it firmly, and let it be until it is healthy;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have already spoken of their cupping and their extraction, which is the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The sanity of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the sanity of the head in ancient diseases of the face, and in migraines, and in redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting, so much that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and press with your hand, or with something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck, and leave the vein until it is healthy and never again will it be swollen from a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it does not seem that the flames should be too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the sanity of transverse, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flames when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The health of the two veins that are in the two arms helps the eyes, and the tongue, and the nostrils, and the little filaments in the eye, and the diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their health is such that the patients strain their neck by twisting in some direction, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the health, and so the healthy part of traversing, a little thick, a little long, a little wide flame, for there is no spot of flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps it breaks;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then make a correction of the blood, as much as you have mastery, and then place it on the cushion, and place it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The health of the vein of the nose is worth ague, and to severe headache, and to diseases of the face, as in migraine and redness that comes into the face, and especially when it is ancient;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the blood is such that the patient strains his neck, then he stretches out his nose to his left hand, and takes a subtle flame long, and fixes it in the lever which is between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well, and the blood will now begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too far in depth, and make the blood flow according to necessity, then leave it for a night, because it is nearly completely restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and that is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the two gums helps with the constriction of the vein, and at the beginning of messelerie, and in many diseases, and in impetigo, and in corroding, and in herpes, and similar things.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the blood is such that the patient strains his neck on one side and then the other, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and be the masters standing over the head of the patient, and the patient sits on the stool, then opens a vein on the arm a little widely, then draws out some blood temperately, or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then reopen another vein, then release the bandage, and hold both veins moderately, so the patient does not strangle;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let it be until morning, so the wound may be healthy.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the veins above the liver helps in the collection at the mouth, and corruption of gums, and cracks of the lips, and painful nose and interior.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the healing is to make the patient sit in front of you, and hold his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the leaf, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right leaf and the other on the left, and you recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins;
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Here is the translation:
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The health of the veins that are beneath the tongue helps after the health of the head, and it is at the narrowing of the throat, and in the diseases of the eye, and in the diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the veins is such that the patient's blood is between your hands before the sun, and lift the tongue, and look underneath on each side for a dark vein;
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	examine one and then the other, and do not press too hard in depth, because beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the neck that are commonly examined are divided into two manners:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	where we prick with a flame making a large scar, or subtly with an olive-shaped instrument as if cutting with a scalpel, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are large and subtle according to the width and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame burning so is very renowned, and it is large as if you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins with a broad, flat needle that appears to contain much blood and turmoil;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and it's the form of the flame of olive oil:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it's more subtly pointed, and is for clearing the subtle veins, where there is subtle citrus blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The juice of the basil, which is one of these veins, helps with the diseases that are beneath the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the vein to bleed slowly, and that it be wary of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a lot of blood comes out, it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and one must not hold the flame in a piercing way, but rather cut skillfully as if with an anvil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basil does not open manifestly, it is necessary that you extract it, and change to another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	where you want no vein of it, where you sensibly feel in his hand the vein within the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the cupping at the flame anus, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to recognize the hand of the wound, it is necessary also that you stretch out the arm, so that you touch the hand as much as you recognize the pulsation;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then signal the hand of the incision, and then stretch out the arm, and cup the vein at the flame anus;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and beware that you do not strike into the artery when you see the hand swollen, for it is an artery:
eschui la donques.	avoid the tendons.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it spout out above like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is not from an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Here is the translation:
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Here is the translation:
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be above fear, and do not move them until they are healthy.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the wound is not cleansed, and it fails you, and the medicine does not present itself to you, then cut open the artery, for the head of the veins retreats.
et estainche li sans.	and cleanse the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a fistula of figs, and apply it, and take one of the embers and lay it well just up to the other joint.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the wound is cleansed, that's good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, then make a cure, as we have said, with powders that cleanse blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the cleansing is not grievous in many dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the possession of the ease of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The health of the vein in a thousand ways helps it draw blood from the head above, and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is necessary for the surgeon to be wary of the nerve that lies beneath, and if he presses too hard in front, and he touches the nerve, and he inflames and the health becomes grievous, and by chance he cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve is exposed many times, and if it does not appear in any men due to its subtlety, it is necessary that you anoint the instrument with oil;
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid touching the nerve with your thumb.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two fingers, then make it bleed far away.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The surgery of the head is helpful, because it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to surgically puncture at the flame of olive or at the flame of myrtle, because it is the safest of all the veins, since there is neither nerve nor artery beneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to choose the lightest hand, and not to hurt anything if one fails the first time, and one recommences;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance inflame the eyes of some men, when they fail at first, but it does not harm anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the health is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about healing is that health is not maintained except by guarding against disease and avoiding future illnesses.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the health be made in one of the three veins that are at the joint:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic, fasting, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must heal at the beginning of taking medicines in spring, and in autumn and in winter after digestion, when the signs of replenishment appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one must heal on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The health that is maintained against diseases has no fixed hour determined, but only when need is of day or night, in all hours and in all tensions;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not suitable to cauterize children until 13 years old, nor a woman carrying a fetus for less than four months until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should they be cauterized, the old who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wants to be cauterized, in whatever way it may be, it is necessary that they empty the intestines with a light clyster, if they have much retained wind, so that the veins do not attract the superfluous and harmful humors from the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor should one be cauterized who is too full of food, nor who is drunk, as long as it may be fervent, nor dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and one should beware of cauterizing after passionate colic, and vomiting, and decay of the stomach, and multiple births for a woman, and labor, watching and fasting, and that which is all virtue, or by means of the arm or gentle body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly balance the humors, if his blood is thick, through food and through drinks and through medications, so you have little power over it;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter into a bath, since nothing can deflect it, to subtly balance the blood, and you will be healthy from the vein of the foot up to the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and beware of that day of labor, and of point, and of luxury, and of similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be gentle and joyful, and let the healthy ones be higher than those whom one heals, and rub the arm two or three times, then gently extract the limb above, for when it is too stretched or short, it cannot correct the blood;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the joint with your hands, until the veins swell, and feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then anoint the healthy ones with a little warm oil, then put his right hand on that vein below the joint a little where it wants to heal, so the vein does not flee and fails to be cauterized.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	Because there are veins that flee like cords to the sainier, and if there are those that are full of windiness, so when one puts on the flame, it draws back from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it opens the vein, so is the wound too narrow, because it is necessary that the surgeons be informed about these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens for the first time, it's good.
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then recommence a little below that place or on the hastening, if the veins are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the veins are swollen, and the patient is in a hurry, let him go for a day or two, and do not tie up the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perhaps he will come to ripen abscesses.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	He does not enter into a bath, then renews his health as it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the perforation is small, where the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it does not issue so much blood as you see, then prick in the same perforation all the way to the right vein;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and let the instrument proceed slowly, so that the veins are not inflamed;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for it often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the vein inflamed, do not renew the health, and put on a little of lukewarm oil, for it alleviates the pain of the blood, and is mixed in this vein with the oil;
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the lukewarm oil to each health that you heal the veins, in order to staunch the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same makes a triangle and bulge of eyes, when one places it on the place;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if the sensation is subtle and separates when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, especially when it is not healthy except at the time or the opening of the vein is small, be quick, and place on the spot a wet sponge in water and boil it slightly hot, and hold for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the flow of blood from the vein, and if it remains on the spot for several days without any blackness or greenness, it does not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, place on something of aloe or myrrh mixed with juice of calendula, mastich, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often there occurs an abscess and appearance at the wound of the basilica:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Put your hand on it, and if you find the soft spot at the compression of the hand, then that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Beware lest you do not put it on anything of what we have said, for perhaps in the short run without an artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but you make a counter-pressure there to harden the spot, then heal with another healing, until it be healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And bleed each one of blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and of the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the wound is black, let it issue forth until it be red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it gross, let it be until it be subtle;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is full and strong, and has mastery of blood extraction, that they make a larger wound, and be the flames large;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and to one who is weak, do the opposite, and it suits them healthier slowly and often, and they must be healed by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of healing is free from deterioration of blood and gathering of nerve, and is worth more than the healing of a long or wide wound.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to one whose body needs healing, it suits to give a soft poultice made from the juice of green apples;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	if it is inflamed, then draw out three or four times the blood; and if it is of cold complexion, then anoint beforehand with a soft poultice in muscat syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he touches the wounded area, after the issue of much blood, it is necessary that he applies a warm poultice of flesh, and a subtle smelling syrup, and uses other things that we have said in the division or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to relieve his arm, and heal another time, it is necessary, when it is weakened by great bleeding, that he be bled little by little, according to the quantity of his continued virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And he who wants to relieve his arm after the first bleeding, and it has a strong course, should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And he who wants to bleed from another part, should be bled on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood within the body that is already inflamed, and it brings on fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if you need to treat a large quantity, and widen the hole as much as it takes in a poultice;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you observe all the signs of health, and place your hand on the pulse when it is healthy, so death does not occur in the poultice, and this happens often, when the healers are negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and do not hesitate when you see the arm relax, and make the blood flow a second time, and the hole is closed, so you press firmly on;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	not if it is curved, that he stretches the arm hastily, for that would be harmful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let it be until it heals a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	where you apply the tip of the flame, until the blood that has congaled at the opening of the vein flows out, and put on the soft skin a little aqua, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is inflamed, let it be and do not constrict it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to bleed twice, if the vein is in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled in the place of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of the healing is such that the patient puts their hand in warm water, so that the vein becomes red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be wrapped moderately, so that the vein appears good, then the wound is now sewn through, not too wide nor too long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the punctures be large, and let it be well sewn near the joint of the hand, and if you cannot get it out, then put the hand in warm water again, and let the blood flow into the water, until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in winter, do not put the hand in warm water again, for one puts it more in ice than in summer;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the healing of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there are neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of the little finger on the right hand is good for all liver diseases, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand, and put it in warm water, until the vein becomes swollen, if you see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if you cross it over, and if you touch it gently all around, so that nothing hurts;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not go too deep in the front, because the nerves are very close to the bare skin, and then put the hand in warm water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot issue forth.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn out blood as much as necessary, then put oil on the vein and sew it up quickly, and thus make a remedy for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The health of the hand on the left side is worth it against the disease of the thigh, and do everything just as I have told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The wisdom of the sapient is worth all the diseases that are beneath the body, as much as diseases of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and disease of the kidneys, and of the hips and ancient legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of his vein is such that the patient puts his foot in warm water, and rubs against the vein until it appears, and lays it above the joint of the foot.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot many roots go forth;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	vein where there is a larger root, or at the ankle, which is more valuable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you make an incision on the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath, and make the incision as in copying.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and be the flames gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the sensation cannot emerge, reset the foot in the water, and let the vein be well cleared.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the surgeons fail the first time, start again a little above, because the sore is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt of nerve, as we have said, and thus make a suture from the same foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The veins of the sciatic leg are at the junction of the thigh, and their surgery is worth the pain of the hip, when it's due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his wound is that the patient will be in a bath, and extract above the Villon III veins by twisting, for otherwise the vein does not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then make an incision in all the ways that you can, and across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is worth more that you copy, because the sore is dry, and it is much restored to many homes.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then there is no healthy vein that opens or closes under the little finger, and towards the small toe, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make the blood flow as you see, and then release the bond, and put on cotton and hold it in place;
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healthy.
des sainies de ventouse	of the veins of the cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Cupping vessels are made of horns, or of antlers, or of glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and cupping is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by striking and attracting blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping that is without striking is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is with fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and cupping that is done by striking and by extraction of blood is done in 14 places on the body, one of which is entirely on the top of the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other is in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and the others are in the hollows of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction underneath the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction on the shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction on the crops;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the suctions in the arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the suctions of the legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the suctions of the ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the suction does not draw out blood, because of the small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason one should not be afraid to do it, as is done with healthy veins;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, neither with full fire nor without sensation of fire, in any disease that comes from excess, as long as the whole body is evacuated.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to suction, or for habitual conditions, one should administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at each time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are those who, when they have the task of bleeding, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who experience fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and there are those who experience a flow of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and spit out blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who sigh, and see nothing but blood and wounds and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the middle of the month, we command to evacuate after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The saliva of the mouth helps with the grief of the head ... that comes to their eyes, and it is not suitable that it be after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this bleeding is in the place of the saliva of the head, and it is not suitable for one who is of a cold complexion or has a catharr, because that does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and because of this it does not seem to me that the old men who have or have had cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who often feels dizzy, becomes oblivious, and therefore it is suitable to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation in the neck is in the place of the healthy head and the basilica, and because of this it is worth to strengthen the foot of the thigh, and to sew up the channel of the forearm, and to touch, and to replenish;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it does not seem to push much, because it holds too firmly, if it injures the obliquity or stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventilations at the ribs of the neck are worth the pains of the head, and obtalmia and emigration, and to constriction, and to the pain as roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the healthiness of the basilica;
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it seems that you instruct the healthy one to press his hand to put, so he does not cut the artery, and does not cause a flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The evacuations below the chin are valid for a disease of the mouth, and for a decay of gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is in the area of the healthy lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilations of the ribs are worth an illness that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The evacuations of the thigh are as valuable as those of the three large veins of the arm, for they attract blood from these thick veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the surgeon to not make too many perforations, for the leg is nourished by flesh, and knows of its lower nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The evacuation that is on the backside is as valuable as hemorrhoids of the fundament, and for diseases below, and it is necessary that the evacuation be large, and be of a kind, so that it has mastery to treat well;
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if it was subtle, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and you make large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The cupping on the legs heals openly, for they attract blood from the whole body, and alleviate ancient pains of the kidneys, and of the liver, and of the bladder, and restore the flowers;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are in the place of two siphons, and of two tubes, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring about gangrene in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply the cup is that you put it on empty, and suck in moderation, and put it on hastily, and remove it equally, and do not cease from doing this, until you see the place red and swollen, and appear the flow of blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then heat, and reapply the cupping, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are those who have such a temperament, and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	it is necessary to cauterize once gently, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a little deep ones;
et suce legierement.	and to suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the wound is large, it is necessary to cauterize twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to subtly open up the way for the large blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the wound is very deep, it is necessary to cauterize a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw out the blood little by little, then we suffice with a single cauterization.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, we recommence often;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the wound is deep, fire in deeply, and the terminations are such that the coursing should be perceived suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have stiff pores, to anoint the keys of the ventouses with opening and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is in this case, of violet oil, or of almond oil sweet, or of oil of cucumber seed;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in Iviera, of oil of cress, or of lily, or of chamomile, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsam, or oil of anise, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one who is applying the fire cautery has a tender and large pores, it does not require putting oil, but it requires washing after the ventilation of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, if he raises from aniseed, or from aqua of myrtle, and of sumac, and of similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have gross superfluities lift themselves with old wine, or water of sage, or decoction of nettle or chamomile, or other similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and do not consider it healthier to apply a cupping glass before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he be warned, when he should be cupped and when he is being cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are healthy and choleric, and their blood is too sharp and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is necessary to take cold things, such as unripe apples and endives and lettuce in the shade, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and mild sauces, and flesh of pheasant, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and mild sauce, and mild sauces and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day when he will be purging, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give to some men three or four draughts of triacle or muscat before purging, or after, to comfort the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the juices be subtle, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The purges that are applied without fear of wounding are those that are applied to the liver, and to the spleen, and to the podagric parts, and to the belly and the bowel and the kidneys and the thighs, for these members cannot suffer wounding on the skin, and one does not do it except to attract blood from member to member, just as we put them on the marmots when the veins are healthy;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	To remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we put cupping glasses on the belly and on the hip to diminish the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is obstruction or stone, if it removes by its attractive virtue by chance the obstruction, or dislodges the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus it does when one puts them on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained viscosity, and these cupping glasses are ministered empty by sucking too strongly;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are ministered together with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in maladies of the pleura, and in such a way that one fills the cupping glass with warm water or hot water where herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping glass administered with fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two large and half palm-width of perforation, and it has or is coated next to the mileu a small hole, just as if to put a needle, and so of arain, soft in front if it does not bother the patient when putting on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and have in hand a rod of across iron or steel, to put a clamp in place, and be they large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the blisters of children are different from those of the old, and of the lean than the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must then put this blister on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the clamp of wax or linen, and put it in the blister across the rod that is in the blister, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the blister, lest it burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the limb, and be careful that it is on the part that we have said, so that when one looks, if the vapor goes away, and remove the blister;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the linen as before, and reapply it often, if you have mastery.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping device which is administered in disease of the lungs, to all aquosity, it has no edge nor perforations, and is not administered unless when it is full of aquosity, and is placed on the limb only so much;
et c’est li forme:	and that's its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Without them being administered unless on members where one cannot put cupping devices due to their smallness, such as eyelids and cheeks, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in the naked parts of the body, such as fingers or toes, and other similar ones;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the usage is that when you find cuppings that are in gentle, sweet, and clear spaces without roughness, if you take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in a gentle and sweet spot, so they become familiar, and have nothing in the way;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be cleansed of vein and cupping, then rub the limb until it becomes red, and put on the bandages;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full, and attract, if it is the place where one can put a cupping, one puts it, for it is very useful afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the place of the axis, and then of water, very well, and then sprinkle;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the places are too sore afterwards along the course of the bandages, so soak a linen cloth in cold water, and put on, until the wounds are strengthened;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the wound is multiple, so put on a vitriol ointment, or warts, and similar things, until it is strengthened;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on the place of soft peas, and let them until they adhere to the place, it will staunch now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you are more skilled, take other sinews.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the sinews do not want to take, rub the joint with fresh blood, or you fix a needle so the sinew goes out, and then put them in place, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will adhere.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they cling, sprinkle on a little of aloe and silk threads, or of powder, they will now adhere.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the foolish mirror lies about this chapter, for they did not find anything in the ancient books, nor did they read any letter.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason is strange the science in our land, because I did not find anything good there.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I knew nothing, except by the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the habituation of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are mentioned, as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the word and the chapters where wisdom places its understanding, and dwells on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a break or dislocation or twist or fracture occurs to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, so that nothing is lacking to you entirely, as weakness of body, or infants, or old people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the tendons are not very strong, or too fragile;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and avoid eating cold joints, it is to know frozen meats, and flesh of birds and goats, and do not drink wine, nor eat raw fat meat, and do not fill oneself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, so that you do not doubt about a hot abscess, nor an expansion of matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient returns to their first government which they have used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to restore, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make great nourishment, or they have viscosity, as if they are strengthened in water, and rice, and bread, and pies, and pork of a calf, and eggs, and fresh fish, and old wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the nourishment represents itself in muscles and soon repairs the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well taken back or rejoined according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those which are too tender, like the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is no cure, reset the broken bone with large tendons which are reunited and join the limb together, so that it strengthens as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not touch the entire area of his work, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish with thick soups, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	Because there is a break that goes to the armpit, and another in adjusting, as the handle of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it breaks with a wound, and breaks into a small crack entirely.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in each manner he has his own engine, and his own instrument proper for restoration, according to what the remembrance brings back to its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the fracture of the bone occurs because the joints are twisted, and appear well by probing, and sound to the pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting in his touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no sign of fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, or crack, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It does not seem that you move to the hand, but put on medications that come here afterwards, and then hold it subtly now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fracture that goes in a curve, and are the two disjointed parts, they must now be put in equal alignment, so that abscesses do not come to life;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses come, let them be, as long as they are quiet, until the abscesses subside;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it in a position where you can lift gently and easily, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restorations of one who has broken pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then restrain it, as it must be afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, whether it is of two parts, it is by hand or foot, or with your hand if it is small members, or with two cords, or with a cord and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are dislocated, you reset them by all means in their proper places as you can, and beware that by your work no harm or injury comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to their best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if you set it straight beautifully, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who make them come by their work causing abscesses and contractions in the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, chastise well the patient so they do not move it, neither while awake nor while sleeping, nor while turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and it is good if the limb is so stabilized that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it's not at all points, and one must put it in such a position that it does not feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and you ensure it is set straight, so that twisting does not come when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken limb's condition is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, like arms and fingers and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	one must envelop them with gentle and subtle drapings;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, like hips and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	one must envelop them with a wide and hard bandage, for wide bands embrace the entire large limb, and hold it steady on all sides equally, so that there is no unevenness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then the interior is stuffed with light poultices, three or four according to the member, and hold your hand a little above all the ligament, then go to the top of the fracture and hold it less, so that the fracture disengages a little.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the ligament little by little, until you grasp a large part of the healthy limb, then take another ligament, and turn again towards the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the fracture, and hold it moderately, not too strongly nor too weakly, as we have said in the first lecture above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the ligaments poultices of linen or drapels, so that it is entirely even, then bind everything above with a bandage, and then place your well-made stitches above, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is inflammation or abscess, apply something soothing to the hot abscess, which reduces the inflammation, and let it be so for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then hold your rods straight, and let them be of the thickness of a large cane reed, or of wood from which one makes writing instruments, or of palm branches, and let them be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the rod which one places on the fracture be a little thicker and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and let it be as long as it is necessary for the size of the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold the rods as you did at the first bandage, then tie them above with a vein-binding thread, just as at the first bandage on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the more tightly it is bound, the less it will be;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be moderate, not too large nor too small, and be of a single mold;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the threads are large, as I have seen the works of foolish people who make their ligatures with twisted cords, and it is a great error, because the ligature cannot be even if it is too subtle, and it is not necessary that there should be less than two inches of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the heads of the stars after being tightened in their healthy places, put beneath them a poultice of linen or a piece of cloth, so that it does not become black.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the courses are broken, I will tell you the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not fitting to tighten the stars all at once on the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, it is not necessary to put these threads further apart than five or seven days, or more according to the severity of the aposteme that is supervening;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and see here the method of the ancient surgeons for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and it is that you take flour that holds as by the walls of the mill, and mix it with abundant egg white, and make this confection, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and it's the common method of the surgeon restoring fractures in many dispositions, and even for women and small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way of restoring plaster for fracture and dislocation and twisting:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	taking Abrams and ladano and enamel and asphaltide and Arabic gum and myrrh, in the name of X;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloe, in the name of V;
alechil VIIII З.;	aloe VIII;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make into powder, and mix with egg white;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the complexion of the man is warm, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is good for many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another way of plaster that is good for twisting:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	taking myrrh and vismalve, in the name of X;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	myrrh and aloe, in the name of VIII;
acaice VI З.;	acacia VI;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Here is the translation:
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way to reset joints and disjointed bones, and appease the sudden pain, and the cutting of the bone, and the fracture:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	take a new linen, and the softness in oil and cooked oil, and put it on the wound.
