puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then put the plaster and bandages on, and place under the belly of the foot a small tablet at the two flat joints, then hold the foot firmly, then you have enveloped the dressing around, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when ten or twelve days will have passed, you should loosen the bandage, because you will find the bones equal, whether they are broken, whether they are dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there are some of the toes broken, restore them, just as we have said about the fingers of the hand.
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then put on the broken toe a splint according to the length of the toe, and let it be a little larger, then place under the foot that tablet that I mentioned, and hold it firmly.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three, or more, broken, set a splint on each joint according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and hold the table steady under the foot;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and let it be standing on the edge of the table away from the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other breaks, since we have spoken.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and attend to each accident as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the break of the bone of the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bone of the thigh in a woman is broken, make her sit enlarged, then incline it towards the back of the spine, and hold it from behind;
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill in the bag with the nature of the patient's cotton, and put therein as large as I stand.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then undress the woman, and lift the back little by little, and then jumps the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of the nature, and returns the bone with the stake.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, if you lift the cloth, and when she has urinated, set it back in place, and do this for seven days or thereabouts:
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	it will restore the fracture, and if you see, take a bladder of birch, and tie it to the perforation with a string, and put all the bladder in the wound;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the string forcefully, until the bladder is inflated inside:
la nature si revenra li brisure;	the wound will restore the fracture;
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for several days, until it is healthy.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the bone of the thumb of a man or woman is broken, restore it in the same way as we have said for the bone of the thigh;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these nearby breaks are not hidden from one who applies his study and practice, and heeds my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture, it indicates in several positions the correct way of restoration:
enten le donques.	Then give instructions.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	On the fracture, when it is broken, take a mouthful of oil and anoint the fracture;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap drapels around, and leave it three days or thereabouts, and it will be quickly healed.
de brisure avec plaie	of breakage with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is fitting for him who has breakage with wound, especially if it is great, such as the bone of the thigh or of the shoulder or similar, that he be healthy now, so that the healings that we have said testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, if the vein of glass, if you have nothing else, then recommence to restore the bruise in the same hour, or that day, so abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come, let the restoration wait until the ninth day, until the abscesses are appeased, and do not touch it on the third day nor on the fourth, for you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears on the uncovered heart, it is necessary that you put it in place lightly with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extensions are not available to put equal in your hands, then reset with this instrument which is of iron, which has seven or eight fingers long, and the width is according to the quantity of the wound;
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and for this reason it is necessary in the mirror that he takes three or four, according to what he needs in each cure of fracture;
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and let it be rounded and a little thick, so that it does not bend under the compression on the member in your work, and let it be smooth in front, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palsy", because it is necessary that the curved head of the bone be placed on top of the apparent os;
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and the joint is once again, so that it regains, and one is equal to the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, it requires that you grasp the head of the bone, so that the instruments have possession of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, then take the handle of an instrument suitable for this, whether it be an incisor or a saw, to your power;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then remove what is stuck in the bone of roughness and of small scars.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is rearranged, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If it does so that it is in its place, then moisten it with wine of a black styptic, and properly if it is in this state;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not put anything on the wound that has oil, lest it cause rot and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer these as you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover it entirely around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constricted with the fracture;
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times they have done this foolishness, and they have brought it upon the patient to death or corruption many a time;
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the strappings be more gentle and softer than the other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident has not occurred, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, then it does not need to be placed on those;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but envelop entirely, in place of these, thick dressings, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see afterwards I or II inflaming the wound, if you remove what you had put on at all cost, and you apply gentle dressings to soothing wounds, as one applies tetrafarmación and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you anoint the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is sound and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs are wrapped in such a way that the bandage does not press too tightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass, and it cannot heal but rather becomes worse, know that there are small pieces of bone, because it is necessary that you touch the wound with a probe, and remove all these separated pieces that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the joint, or another kind of corruption, then it is necessary that you cure it, according to what is stated in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken, and opens into the limb, like the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not treat it, for many times death ensues, but let it be until it suppurates;
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	perhaps it will fall out by itself after 20 days or 30, then cure the wound, if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	the bruises that come upon the skin
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often come across this after the health of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a difficult thing to see the shape of the limb;
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and sometimes cannot make the limbs perform their natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take heed therefore when it is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if you administer stippling medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, acaice, and similar others, so that you take none of these things, or all together, and conflate them with wine stippling or with abundant water or with oil;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and put them on the affected area in a poultice, and hold it well, and do not dislodge it for many hours;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then remove it, and restart with another, until the swelling is gone;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	where you hold onto a well-made wooden splint;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of wood is that it removes all swelling from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the nodulation is already converted into hardness like a stone, and it needs to be removed, so scrape above it, and make the surplus apparent;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	where you take it to a skilled surgeon, until it is removed, and the treatment until it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of a limb that is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and remains afterwards with weak and subtle limbs, it happens for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	because one is that it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because there were too many bindings, and could not bring nourishment to the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	where for a multitude of arrangements;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	where for too great movements, do not trouble him at his hour;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	where because he has little blood in his body, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the treatment is that you should make the patient lean, and make the body tender, so that the blood is multiplied in him;
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer a bath, and give joy and happiness;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then apply poultice on the limb, if the poultice attracts to the great nourishment, and the arrangement often draws out tedious water, until the nourishment runs to the limb;
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and restores it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	because of a twisted limb after the injury
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after the restoration, and the broken bones are open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	do not believe the fools who say one must break the limb entirely anew, and many foolish physicians have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this practice is blamed, and great evils come from it, and sometimes death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	however, if the nodations and torments are fresh, it is necessary that they be raised with warm water, or mollifying herbs be applied, such as leaves of vismalve, and roots, and mellilot, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and make a mollifying plaster, as one makes diachylon well, and take the mucilage of vismalve, and mix it with grease of goose or oil of sisamont, and apply the plaster thus;
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or you take fat figs, and crush them with flour of Colonne, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And at no time is the node removed by constantly and continually rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let the member be moved gently every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the twistedness is enveloped and hardened, just like a stone, and it needs to be opened with the iron, so it should be covered just up to the bone, at the subtle incision site lightly.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and apply cauterization and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, if it is necessary to now bring back into alignment.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if we delay, the eyes will inflame, and perhaps by chance they will reset into their proper place;
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	because it is not suitable to move it at the hour when it is inflamed:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times it brings on spasms and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	in any case, when this happens, make the patient healthier, then leave him, until the aposteme (abscess) becomes calm;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the member with warm water and oil, then reset it lightly, and treat each member as the treatment will come into its proper place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the limbs from head to foot.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	Sometimes it happens that the jaws are dislocated and swollen, and the dislocation of the arms is in two ways:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	where they are a little out of their joints, and softened a little;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	where they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the chest, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so it cannot hold it, nor can it close its mouth, and entangles its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns to its natural positions more easily.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is entire and complete, then you must reset it quickly, and do not delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the minister holds the head of the patient, and puts his fingers like a pouch in one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two fingers of the hand be bent back, to make even;
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to soften them, their jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fingers put it even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if the reset is rough, meanwhile it is the two jaws together, if they are washed with warm water and oil, so that they reset lightly;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not delay the reset, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well without becoming soft, then place a moistened cloth made of rose oil and wax, then tie it lightly with many bands.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the patient sleep on their back, and their head be between two pillows, so that they do not move to the right or left, nor exert themselves too much, but take light food, until the pains are alleviated, and the jaws are relaxed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then advise him to eat lightly, and not struggle much to open his mouth to the morsel and to the drink, so that the jaw be well set and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be adjusted to a point at one hour, and are not converted to their proper places, then fever and excessive sweating come, and by chance a loose bowel, and by chance a vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is a perilous condition;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times dies the one who has it, in eight days.
de la forcelle	of the force
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The force cannot dislodge the rib from its continuity and from the breast, and it is often dislodged at the fracture, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies comfortably on his back, and stretches out his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on the plaster and the bandage, and bind it tightly;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the head which is towards the side cannot be dislocated;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does not, and if it dislocates again, you should reset it to its place, as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then put on the plaster and the bandage, and hold it steady, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healthy.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and thus the same is reset the head of the spine, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is not dislocated except in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	because one of them is that it dislocates towards the back part at the joint;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is towards the front of the thigh;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and sometimes it dislocates upwards, and that happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and it does not dislocate backwards because of the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inward because of the veins;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and often it dislocates downwards towards the joint, especially in those who have little flesh, because for them it happens suddenly;
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	For those who have enough flesh, it pierces at points, and re-enters at points.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that they receive a blow or fracture, and the shoulder is inflamed with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	It is necessary therefore that you test them, as long as you are certain of them;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that dislocations occur when it falls towards the joint, and makes a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among them a manifest diversity;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and below the joint, touching the head of the shoulder, as if it were a bone;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor move with any movements;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and thus, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it manifestly at the joint;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this manner of dislocation is not forcing to recall, when it is new, or if the veins are diseased.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the ministers lift the hand of the patient upwards high, then put their fingers underneath the shoulder blade, and lift the joint with force upwards to its place;
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the ministers lift the hand, and stretch it upwards, then put it underneath;
si venra hastanment.	if it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said in many days afterwards, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in warm water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the minister applies soothing and calming remedies, such as a decoction of lettuce and fenugreek and melilot in warm water, and it is soothed;
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then the patient is laid on their back, and a strip of linen cloth, not too soft nor too hard, is placed underneath the shoulder blade, then the minister places their heel on the strip, and lifts the head of the shoulder strongly, and draws the hand of the patient;
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another minister touches the head of the patient, so that he does not move downwards;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	that shoulder returns now entirely, and if you see whether it is reset according to this method:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and it is that you make the bone which is more massive than the patient's;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and be straight towards the ribcage, and push the shoulder down to the bone of the patient's, and lift the bone high up, so that the patient's arm hangs in the air;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another minister draws the patient's hand downwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too lightweight, then weigh him down with something heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And it is reset in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is as if one fixes a long pole on the ground, so that the head is also straight like a pestle, and neither too large nor too slender;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it should be placed under the patient, but so that it has soft drapery above, and the patient is standing straight from the long pole of the beam;
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then let his hand be extended downward from the other part in a straight line, and the joint will quickly return to its place.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then make this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take a stick of two feet in length and four fingers in width, which has the top end rounded to enter obliquely into the hollow of the joint, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then place the top end of the stick wrapped in cloths, so that the stick does not touch the patient, then put it under the joint of the patient;
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend the arm along the length of the stick, and place the shoulder on the stick, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on a small stool of a chair, and let the hand be extended downward, and let the body hang from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the joint returns to its place now
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, whatever way it may be, it is necessary that you place under the seat a layer of even linen, then put on top the plaster made from powder of soft millet, with incense and album of egg white, across the entire shoulder and around, then hold under the seat firmly, and turn the ligature on the plaster, and bind the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary to nourish a little, as long as the limb is comforted, for it will heal more quickly;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then nourish more afterwards 5 or 7 days, and move it;
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is strengthened and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture or another cause, then it is necessary that you administer cauterizations at three points, as it is described before in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after 7 days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift its arm above, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is affected or stretched out or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is towards the chest, and the breasts, or behind, if made by impulse, and stretching of hands, and it needs another treatment.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal as long as he is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the healing comes numbness to the limb, and later on it has difficulty in movement, if the patient bathes many times, so that this numbness is alleviated, and it returns to its original nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation where it hurts
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Know that the joint of the hip is dislocated to points, and at points returns;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and it is dislocated in all parts, and meanwhile before and behind, and the dislocation is not fully restored, for one sees well and feels well;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the injured limb with the healthy one, then it can be seen openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is crooked, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary that you reset it thus so that abscesses do not gather there, for if abscesses gather there, it would be grievous to reset;
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and perhaps it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is behind;
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	if it is worse than the other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And the restoration is, when it is such that one can reset it, that you extend your hand to your two hands;
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and his arms should be expansive, and the hands soft in the mirror according to the count of the interior, above and below, and bent the jointure at his fingers assembled, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when it doubles its hand to its hand, and fixed from the root of the palm the bend that was dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and they hold two ministers, so that it does not move at extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm of each part, then you have enveloped a double layer long and wide;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the mirror joins the jointure to his hand, if you anoint it with some oil to mollify the jointure, then bent the jointure forcibly, until it returns;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in its place, if you put a dry plaster on with egg white, and hold it firmly, and bend the arm at the neck of the patient, and leave it for some days, then dislocate it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	And if the joint is fixed in its place, then disentangle the ligament, and let it go.
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint does not fix well, then reapply the poultice and the ligament, and let it go thus for some days, until it is firmly set;
puis le deslie.	then disentangle it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if he feels grittiness after the reset of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub well, and press until it is alleviated;
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	where you put on the joint a fatty woolen cloth of sheep, then let it be for a day and a night, then remove it, and make it enter into a bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when it sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put the woolen cloth back on, and then enter into a bath;
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and thus do it two or three times until he is healthy;
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see that, put a warm poultice of soft butter on it, and hold it in place;
si revenra a sa disposition.	if it returns to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and the return is easy, more so than the other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it is necessary to return it to its place quickly, in the same way that it was dislocated, so that the limbs are not swollen, or an abscess does not form there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the way to return it is that you put the injured hand on a table, and stretch out the fingers of the hand, and the doctor puts them in alignment, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and presses until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, you go ahead, it is necessary to examine if it is well in its place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	then put the patient's hand on a table at extension and at flexion.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then place the patient's hand on the table, and the doctor places his hand on the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then strain the emplasters calming abscesses and let them sense re-commence.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it in its place after several days, the twisted joint remains.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and do not annoy the patient further unless the hand is numb, and cannot strain anything at all:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	then know that the nerves are injured, or the arteries;
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	if there is no other remedy except to strain by cauterization in this case, and by chance it will not be worth anything else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is on the spot, put on the plaster that we have mentioned, then hold it and leave it thus for a while, then remove it and leave it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is no grinding, then soak the swollen area in warm water, and rub it so that it becomes healthy.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Never are the fingers of the hand dislocated to any part, never to the back of the palm or to the belly;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then they are the fingers, and push the dislocation to your pouches as long as it returns, then support the head of the finger, and bend towards the part where it is disjointed;
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and let it go immediately, and then put it even with that joint;
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and bind the limb, as we have said, and release the joint, and make it move, and rebind the limb;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do it often, until it is straight, and do everything thus, if it is dislocated at the belly of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healthy;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do everything thus, when it is dislocated from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	for the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, where there are multiple dislocations, if there is no point of healing, because death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the evacuations suddenly burst forth with great force, cannot be held back, and often some member is softened, either the two hips or the two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And often the shinbone changes to four parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	that which changes at the back is called "gilbositez";
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	the treatment is that you should rewarm where the gilbositez has come from childhood:
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is no cure or healing of the entire body.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falls or blows or similar things, the ancient ways of cures used big words, where there is no great profit in all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the gilbositez that comes at the worst front, there is no engineer who can heal it;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and thus it is that which comes straight to the II costal, and one cannot cure fevers except that which comes properly to the back, if I say so;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient should be stretched out on their face in a level place, and have support beneath him, so he does not slip;
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then fix the cushion under the head on the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a bandage beneath the patient's hips, and another at the thighs, and at the knees, and at the ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and two ministers should tighten the bandages, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the two cushions;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and they should be well fastened, the cushion as we have said, and the mirrors place their palms on the spine firmly, until it recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a tube of three feet in length, and place the tip beneath the patient's back, and let the patient be on their side, and insert the head of the tube beneath the patient's back, then put the middle of the tube on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and place the mirrors at their feet on the other end of the tube, and press well, until it returns to its place;
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see, then make it so that the turnet turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you fix two tensors at the head of the patient's arm, and towards the feet two others, and between each tensor, above and below, a palm's width of space;
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and have in each tensor a hole, where the turnet runs, and let the tensors be firmly on the ground, so that they do not move;
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each II of them a torn ligament, for which the torn ligament turns, and has in II turners II small torn ligaments of a palm's length, to turn the turning handle;
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then the ligament that is among the bones to the turning handle towards the head, and the other ligament towards the feet at the other turning handle, and each of the ministers turns their turning handle to all the ligaments, and the masters set the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, then set on an emplaster of decumatif with a lot of egg white, and then the poultices, and then the stellate of a tablet of three fingers' length, which grips the limb of the gibbosity and the part of the healthy spine, then tie with a ligament, as we have said, and use the subtle remedies of nourishment, until it is sane;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if some thing comes at the end of the health, it is necessary to administer soothing and softening medicines, with the steel that we have mentioned before;
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	and sometimes I administer on a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance comes in the back of the dorsal spine, and think that it is dislocations;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and it is the bone that opens, because one should not have mistaken judgment:
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	perhaps it may bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocations of the thigh
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only come to be dislocated solely, not so like the other joints;
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to three parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	downwards and upwards, and forwards and backwards;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and more downwards than the haunches, and a little dislocated forwards and backwards.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation is that when one joins the injured leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens more the injured knee than the healthy one, and the injured one cannot bend its knee by fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the loosened flesh that is inflamed from a hot abscess, because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the signs of the one who is near death, if it is that these accidents are contrary to those beforehand.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of the one who has it in front, it is that they stretch their leg according to its fulfillment;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	anyway, do not bend the knee without pain, and if you want to make it move, it cannot go forward, and holds back its urine, and inflames the groin, and when it goes, it passes over the ankle.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of the one who is behind, if it is that he cannot stretch his knee, nor double, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the thigh is at the level of the ribs beneath the costs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	The reminders of this kind of dislocation are that you should rewind if the dislocation is old, and it stays according to its disposition, so there is no cure.
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and it does not seem that he has a good prognosis.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is one of the three ways of dislocation, if you hurry to put the joint back in place, and stretch it within and without, and move it to the right and left;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	perhaps it will recover, and there is no need for another treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not recover in this way, then you must prepare the limb strongly, and hold the leg firmly with both hands, or tie it with a bandage around the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and another minister stretches his hand above in this manner so that he presses his hands under his haunches, then tightens a soft bandage around the hip;
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another pulls the head of the bandage;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch upwards and downwards all at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four similarities, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If this does not occur, then one must apply treatment to its similarity.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the shoulder, then you must place the patient on their healthy side, then put the bandage at the root of the hip, and the joint that is below the angle, then extend the bandage upwards towards the angle, and towards the strength.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then take another minister by his arms, and embrace the large joint of the hip that is diseased, and extend it to its former shape.
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	if it returns to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this manner of dislocation is easier than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot hold it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft bandage on the two heels, and on the two knees, and so the diseased leg is extended two fingers more than the others.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then let it be hung on a wooden pole, and let it be two cubits above the ground in length.
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then instruct the minister to embrace the head of the hip, and let another minister be hung with the patient, who firmly embraces the hip, because the joint returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is in default, thus guide the patient, as we have said in the one who has a clubfoot, and straighten the ligament on the affected leg properly, and on the foot also.
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then put two splints, one at the head and another at the feet, then fix the splint between the hips of the patient in the form.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have wet cloths applied around, so that they do not blister the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and the mirrors place equally with their hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If she returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put him on the table, and press thus as we have said in the gibosity, and adjust the patient to the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch the affected leg quickly, and according to what I have said.
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and put the fingers of one hand on the affected joint, then press with the other hand, and stretch downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is backwards, it is not necessary to stretch the affected part downwards, nor to lift from the ground, but rather it should be as if the joint were dislocated backwards, just as we have said about the positioning on the two hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and it should be on its face, and the bandage stretched out as we have said before, and one must press on the joint at the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and it will be at a point when the patient stretches his legs, and they will be equal.
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then adjust the hips, and apply the plaster, and bind with a bandage, so that the hip does not move.
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and let it rest for three days or four, then dislodge it, and put the plaster on;
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are even, hold steady, as before, and let it be for three days;
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then dislodge it, and make the patient walk gently, until the limb is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The knee is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	it is to know, inward and forward, and backward;
et ne desalue point devant.	and do not dislocate at all in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg to their thigh, and if it does not adhere to their thigh, know that it is dislocated;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg as they can, and place your back against their face, and put their foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	Then take your knee in your palms, and draw it back between your thighs, then bend the two sides of the knee in a circular shape.
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and another minister extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the signs are that he has well aligned his leg with his hip lightly.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and put the plaster on, and make the leg adhere to the hip, and bind them together strongly for three or four days, then remove it.
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and do not disturb the patient's pain further, until the limbs are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not at all, if administration is strongly extended, as we have said in the treatment of the ankle, until it be healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankles are sometimes sprained and sometimes completely dislocated, and inwardly and outwardly.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the swelling is reduced, and stretch beforehand to the part where it was dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The reminiscence is lighter, and one must extend it lightly with their hands when it is slightly swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is completely dislocated, it is necessary that you make the patient sit upright, and hold one minister firmly by the leg, above the swelling.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then prick the foot with your right hand, and then with the left twice, then hold it high, and push the foot up high;
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pricking the foot;
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	if it returns, that's good;
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	if not, then restart the work, for it returns;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return thus, then make the patient sit on his back on the ground, and fix the pillow firmly on the ground between his thighs, and wrap the drapery around, so that the patient does not slip;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then hold the minister's thigh, and another minister stretches out the foot with his hands or with a strap, so that it lies on the neck of the foot;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then each minister stretches out evenly, and the pillow should be placed between the thighs of the patient to retain the patient when one holds them;
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then set the mirrors equal to the dislocation with his hands, and another minister touches the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is at the point, set the plaster and bandages above, and hold firmly, and place the foot on the leg, and guard the veins that are on the back of the knee, so that the ligaments do not become too stretched.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligaments soften, hold it firmly.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	Then loosen it on the third day or on the fourth, and forbid the patient to move for four days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes beyond that term, it is not certain that he will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses or wounds come, it is necessary that you touch them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healthy.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the fingers are dislocated, it is necessary to stretch them nicely without strain, and it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any of the two toes or feet, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a straight table, and put your foot on what opens from these joints, then press your foot firmly, until it returns to its place.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when it is even, and there appears nothing, if you put under the foot a flat table to support the head, then you restrain strongly, and let it be for three days, then you release;
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and make it rest, until it is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with a dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the cure, be wise in the art and you have not used it for a long time, and be piteous and merciful and slow, not harsh;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and apply gentle remedies at the beginning of hot abscesses, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you do not see hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the hot abscesses will not return;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is out of place, if you administer soothing remedies to the inflamed abscess, and treat the wound, as it is fitting, with dry dressings.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and also with a fracture or breakage, and less severe dislocations, if you reduce the swelling, and do what we have said about simple illnesses.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and beware of entering into a path of fear, according to what I have said, for it will be of no value to you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arm and your body.
